Problem Statements by Vertical
Four core pain points for each practice type — with one-line hooks for outreach and discovery
Med Spa
Cosmetic Dermatology
Plastic Surgery
Wellness Centers
Med spa owners are running a high-consideration business where patients need to imagine themselves in the results before they'll commit. Most never do. They browse before-and-afters of strangers, feel nothing personal, and disappear. Your existing patients got Botox once and haven't been back. Your ad leads show up cold, price-sensitive, and skeptical. And your front desk can't run a disciplined follow-up cadence on top of everything else they're managing. You have a visualization and execution problem, not a traffic problem.
Four core pain points
New patients not booking
8 out of 10 people who want Botox, fillers, or laser and can afford them never book. They leave without ever imagining themselves in the result.

Existing patients not returning
Your database is full of patients who came in once, trusted you, and disappeared. Nobody showed them what's possible next.

Leads not converting
Ad spend generates names and phone numbers. No intent data, no qualification, no way to tell a serious buyer from a tire-kicker before staff spends 45 minutes finding out.

Follow-up execution gap
Front desk staff can't run a disciplined lead cadence. Leads go cold in the first hour because no one owns follow-up with a real process behind it.

Signature play for medspa
Their own face is the only face that converts
Medspa is the purest version of the visualization problem in aesthetics. Every practice runs ads. Every practice posts before-and-afters on Instagram. Every practice fills a contact form. And 8 out of 10 qualified patients still don't book — because browsing a stranger's result doesn't create commitment to your chair.

Ageless closes the gap by moving the "after" onto the patient's own face. A paid social click lands on a visualization of her own lips with filler. A waiting-room QR code shows him his own jawline after Ulthera. Her Botox patients see themselves with filler they've never tried. The conversion mechanism is identity — and no competitor lets you do that at this price point.

One-line hooks
New patients:
"Your patients are browsing before-and-afters of strangers. They'll never book based on someone else's face."
Existing patients:
"What percentage of your Botox patients have ever tried filler? Most practices don't know — because nothing ever showed those patients what was possible."
Lead quality:
"If your staff can't tell a five-star lead from a browser before picking up the phone, they're spending half their day on the wrong people."
Follow-up:
"How many touches does your team make before giving up on a lead? Most practices stop at two. The data says it takes seven or eight."
Cosmetic dermatology practices live in two business models under one roof — an insurance-based medical practice and a cash-pay aesthetic practice — and the seam between them is where revenue leaks. Medical patients sit in exam rooms for twenty minutes of idle time and never learn that the same doctor treating their eczema also does Botox. Aesthetic patients arrive over-researched, credential-skeptical, and ready to comparison-shop. And the follow-up cadence that cosmetic leads require is completely foreign to a clinical operation trained on insurance authorizations, not sales sequences.
Four core pain points
Medical-to-aesthetic cross-sell invisible
Your medical patients trust you with their skin already. They sit in your waiting room and exam rooms with idle minutes on their phones. Most have no idea the same doctor offers Botox, fillers, or laser. The cross-sell opportunity is sitting in the room — nobody is activating it.

Aesthetic patients arrive over-researched
Cosmetic dermatology patients do more homework than any other aesthetic buyer. They arrive with screenshots, comparison notes, and a list of credentials. Without a personalized outcome they can see on their own face, they leave to keep shopping.

Leads not converting
Cosmetic leads from ads are price-shopping three practices simultaneously and arrive with no emotional commitment to your clinic specifically. Credentials alone don't close — visualization does.

Clinical staff can't run sales follow-up
Medical assistants are trained on insurance authorizations and clinical intake, not sales cadences. Cosmetic inquiry follow-up has no owner, no cadence, and no system behind it — so it doesn't happen.

Signature play for cosmetic derm
The waiting-room cross-sell
Cosmetic dermatology has something no medspa has: existing clinical patients physically sitting in your practice with idle time on their hands. Exam room waits. Lobby waits. Post-procedure recovery windows. Every one of those moments is an untapped cross-sell surface — and they're surfaces a practice owns, not ones that have to be bought through paid media.

Deploy Ageless as an in-office experience: a branded standee with a QR code in the waiting area, a tablet in the exam room, a screen behind the check-in desk. A medical patient waiting to be seen for acne or eczema scans the code, uploads a selfie, sees themselves with Botox or laser, and walks into the exam room already asking about it. The conversion happens before the doctor ever brings up cosmetic services — which removes the awkwardness of upselling inside a clinical visit.

The surface area is free. The patients are already there. Ageless turns idle waiting-room minutes into your highest-converting cross-sell channel.

One-line hooks
Waiting-room cross-sell:
"Your patients spend twenty minutes in your exam rooms before they see you. Right now that time is dead space. Ageless turns it into your highest-converting cross-sell surface."
Medical-to-cosmetic:
"Your medical patients are the warmest cosmetic prospects you'll ever have. They already trust you with their skin. They just don't know what else you offer — and the current workflow has no moment to tell them."
Brand posture:
"This isn't a medspa tool bolted onto a medical practice. It's a patient-facing experience designed for clinical settings — premium, discreet, and branded to your practice, not to ours."
Aesthetic conversion:
"Dermatology patients research harder than any other aesthetic buyer. Credentials don't close them — seeing their own face does."
Lead quality:
"Every cosmetic lead from your ads is talking to two other practices. The one who shows them their own face first wins."
Follow-up:
"Your medical assistants aren't trained to run sales follow-up cadences — that's not a staff problem, it's a system problem. Ageless handles it automatically."
Plastic surgery practices are built on surgical volume, but the majority of patient indecision — and unrealized revenue — lives in the non-surgical layer. Patients exploring that layer need a conversion mechanism that matches their commitment level. Without it, they leave. Patient coordinators focused on surgical scheduling have no bandwidth to fix it.
Four core pain points
Non-surgical pipeline leaking
Most patients researching plastic surgery start with non-surgical options. There's nothing on your site to capture them at that stage before they move on.

Existing patients not returning
Post-surgical patients in maintenance mode have the highest lifetime value in the practice. Nobody is showing them what's possible next.

Consultation quality
Non-surgical consults are low-commitment for patients, which makes them low-conversion for staff. Patients arrive curious, not committed.

Follow-up execution gap
Patient coordinators are consumed by surgical scheduling. Non-surgical lead follow-up has no owner and no cadence.

Signature play for plastic surgery
The non-surgical bridge to the surgical consult
Plastic surgery practices are built on surgical volume — but most surgical patients don't start their journey wanting surgery. They start curious about Botox, filler, or laser, and they work their way up the commitment ladder over months. Your practice needs a mechanism that captures them at that exploratory stage, converts them into a non-surgical relationship, and nurtures them toward the surgical consult when the time is right.

Ageless is that bridge. Patients see themselves refreshed with non-surgical treatments on day one, book a smaller consult to get started, and enter a long-term relationship with your practice — so that when they're ready for rhinoplasty, blepharoplasty, or a facelift, you're the obvious choice because the trust is already built. And with surgical visualization launching in June 2026, the practices that deploy Ageless now will have the patient relationships ready when it arrives.

One-line hooks
Non-surgical pipeline:
"Your non-surgical pipeline is the entry point for surgical patients. Right now, most of them are leaving before they ever get that far."
Consultation quality:
"If a patient arrives not knowing what they want, your team is a salesperson. If they've already seen their result, your team is a closer."
Future positioning:
"Surgical visualization is coming in June 2026. The practices positioned now will have the patient relationships ready when it launches."
Follow-up:
"What happens to a non-surgical inquiry that doesn't respond to the first call? In most practices, it quietly disappears."
Wellness sells the hardest thing in healthcare: a six-to-twelve-month commitment to an invisible process. Generic before-and-afters of other people don't move wellness patients — they don't identify with a stranger's weight-loss photo or someone else's body recomp. What moves them is seeing
themselves
at the finish line. The before-and-after is a forty-year-old concept in aesthetics because it works; what makes it convert for wellness is when the after is the patient's own face and their own body. That's the emotional commitment wellness has been missing — and it's what Ageless delivers.
Four core pain points
New patients not starting the program
GLP-1, hormone, and peptide programs are 6-to-12-month commitments. Patients inquire, hear the price and the timeline, and ghost. They can't emotionally commit to a finish line they can't picture themselves at.

Early churn before results arrive
Wellness patients drop off in weeks 3 to 8 because progress is invisible. Scale hasn't moved enough. Energy hasn't shifted yet. Without a clear picture of where they're headed, they quit before the results are real.

Curious buyers vs. motivated buyers
Wellness leads skew toward curious and hopeful. Staff can't separate motivated patients from passive researchers without spending an hour on the phone first — and in programs this long, that qualification gap is expensive.

Clinical teams running sales cadences
Wellness conversions take 7 to 10 touches. Clinical staff aren't trained or equipped to run that cadence — which isn't a staff failure, it's a system gap. Without automation behind the follow-up, most leads die in the first week.

Signature play for wellness
Aspiration on their own body — not a stranger's
The before-and-after isn't a new concept. It's been the core conversion tool in aesthetics for forty years because aspiration drives action. What's new is whose body the "after" lives on. For decades the industry has shown patients photos of someone else at the finish line and asked them to identify with it. Most don't. And in wellness specifically — where the commitment is six to twelve months of injections, lab draws, lifestyle change — identification with a stranger isn't enough to anchor that commitment.

Ageless moves the "after" onto the patient's own face and body. A GLP-1 prospect sees herself at her goal weight on day one. A TRT prospect sees himself with the body recomp result before he books the consult. A hormone patient sees her energy and vitality visualized on her own features. The emotional response is different in kind, not degree — it's the difference between wanting something and picturing yourself having it.

That shift is what converts the 6-month commitment. Patients who can see themselves at the finish line start the program and stay in it. Patients who can't, don't.

One-line hooks
The category reframe:
"Before-and-afters have worked in aesthetics for forty years because aspiration converts. What's missing in wellness is whose body the 'after' lives on. Ageless puts it on the patient's own face."
GLP-1 / weight loss:
"A GLP-1 program is a six-month commitment. If she can't see herself at her goal weight on day one, she's not starting the program — she's price-shopping."
Hormone / TRT:
"Men don't browse before-and-afters of other men's faces. They want to see themselves stronger. Show them their own body recomp result and they'll book."
Early churn:
"Patients quit in weeks 3 to 8 because they can't feel progress yet. Showing them the finish line — on their own body — is how you carry them through the gap between starting and seeing results."
Lead quality:
"How much time does your team spend on consultations with patients who never start a program? In a 6-month-commitment category, that's the biggest hidden cost you have."
Follow-up bandwidth:
"Wellness conversions take 7 to 10 touches. Most clinical teams get to 2 or 3. That's not a sales failure — it's a bandwidth problem only automation solves."
Ageless Call Flow
End-to-end playbook for Ageless demo calls — built from what's worked across 27 calls in the War Room. A flow, not a script. Adapt to the prospect, don't recite.
Overview
1. Before the call
2. Discovery
3. Demo
4. Admin
5. Pricing
6. Close
7. Objections
This is a
call flow
, not a script — the difference matters. A script assumes every prospect is the same and every call runs the same steps in the same order. A call flow gives you the spine plus branches for when the prospect in front of you isn't the default shape. The best calls in our dataset don't follow a script — they follow a flow, adapt in the first 5 minutes based on what they're hearing, and close with a handful of reusable moves.
The six sections of every call
1
Before the call — 5 minutes of prep
Research the website, socials, and RMD dashboard if existing customer. Identify archetype. Prepare one specific opener tied to research. Five minutes of prep is the difference between generic and specific — and prospects can tell.
2
Discovery — 8 to 15 minutes depending on prospect shape
This is where calls are won or lost. Five archetype tracks determine your opener and drill sequence. Five universal drill moves apply on every call regardless of archetype. Bridge to demo when the prospect's story is complete, not when your list is complete.
3
Demo — patient flow, admin, enrichment
30-second pre-demo config check. Patient flow walkthrough. Comprehension check at the 5–7 minute mark. Aging flow for the emotional hook. Wellness flow only if they offer it.
4
Admin & enrichment
Dashboard walkthrough, star rating system, AI enrichment surface, messaging modes, CRM integration pause.
5
Pricing
Three tiers, rollover bank, overage mechanics, waitlist context as leverage. Canadian prospects: CAD disclosure upfront before the tiers.
6
The close — including sign-up-and-pause
Founders club offer.
Sign-up-and-pause as required equipment
when timing is the blocker. Card on call is the gold standard. Reciprocal follow-up as the backup.
What this document assumes about you
You know the product. You've watched a few of the Gong recordings in the War Room. You're willing to get specific instead of generic. You can sit with silence after you ask a question. Discovery is a skill being developed, not a checklist to complete — Matt's 3 questions are a floor, not a ceiling.
Five minutes of prep before the call is the difference between generic and specific. It's also the clearest signal to the prospect that you did the work. Prospects can tell when a rep did homework and when they didn't. Homework buys you the permission to get specific in discovery.
Minimum prep — 5 minutes
Research
Their website — 2 minutes
Scan the services menu, location, any named physicians, any visible tech (VISIA, Podium, Growth99, Aura, Zenoti). Look for one specific detail you can reference in the first 3 minutes of the call.
Research
Their socials — 1 minute
Instagram. Posting style, before-and-after shots, follower count, what they emphasize. You're not researching them to pitch them back at them — you're researching to understand their voice before you talk to them.
Research
Existing RepeatMD customer? Pull the dashboard
Revenue, member count, transaction volume. You should be able to cite a specific number. Zack's Becky call opened with "you're doing about $5K/month in membership revenue" — and that opener produced a card-on-call close. The dashboard is the fastest way to prove you did the work.
Decision
Identify the archetype
Before the call starts, make a guess: existing RMD customer, cold practice owner, values-forward MD-led, channel partner, or pre-sold warm inbound. See the Discovery tab for the archetype map. Your opener changes based on which of these you're talking to.
Prepare
One specific opener tied to the research
Not flattery. Not a rehearsed line. Something from your research that lets the prospect teach you something.
Examples from the dataset:

•
"I was looking at your site — you've got a pretty complete menu. I'm curious about your Moxie laser program specifically."
(Shawn)

•
"You're in Niagara on the Lake — beautiful area. I saw you also have a location attached to a hotel?"
(Jen Platinum)

•
"I see you've got VISIA in practice — how's that working for you?"
(Yaman / Jen Platinum)

•
"I'm looking at your dashboard and you're doing about $5K/month in membership revenue. That's solid."
(Becky — existing RMD)
Discovery is not a list of questions to run through. It's a conversation where you follow the prospect's lead and drill into what they volunteer. The information you need will come out if you let them talk and ask specific follow-ups to what they say. Five archetype tracks plus five universal drill moves.
The archetype map — first question branches here
Track A
Existing RepeatMD customer
Signal:
They show up in the RMD database. You've pulled their dashboard data.

Opener:
Skip "tell me about your business." Open with specific dashboard data. This is Zack's Becky move.

"Hey, before we dive in — I was looking at your dashboard. You're doing about [X] in membership revenue and you've got [Y] members. That's working well. What made you want to look at Ageless specifically?"

Why it works:
You're confirming, not asking. You've proven you did the work. You're opening the door for them to tell you what the gap is — which is where Ageless fits.
Follow-up drills:
Where's the biggest gap in the patient journey — booking, showing, converting? Any churn back on memberships? What have you tried for new patient acquisition recently?
Track B
Cold / new practice owner — standard shape
Signal:
Not in RMD. Standalone practice or newly-bought. Could be medspa, MD-led, or NP-owned.

Opener:
Research-anchored question that shows you looked.

"I was on your site — you've got [specific thing]. Walk me through the business a little. How long have you been running it, and what's your main patient flow today?"
Follow-up drills:

• "How are patients finding you right now?" — don't accept "word of mouth" as the full answer. Drill:
"When someone's referred, what do they do — call, book online, walk in? How does that first touch happen?"

• "When they find you, who's managing the follow-up?"

• "What's your current conversion rate from first contact to first appointment? Do you know?"
Track C
Values-forward MD-led or NP-led practice
Signal:
Website language emphasizes "empowerment," "celebrate yourself," "your natural beauty," or similar. Often has an MD/NP who writes personally on the site. Often focused on "under-promise, over-deliver" as a stated philosophy.

Opener:
Softer. Don't lead with acquisition metrics — lead with philosophy.

"I read through your site — your approach to patient care comes through pretty clearly. I want to understand how you're thinking about growth while protecting the practice's philosophy. Can you walk me through how you bring new patients in today?"

Why it works:
You're signaling you read the site for real. You're not treating this like a metrics conversation. You're inviting them to explain their values, which is the most important data on the call.
Pre-empt the beauty score objection:
Before you get to the demo, mention the toggle.
"One thing to know — we have a beauty score feature and some practices love it, some turn it off. Totally configurable. I'll show you both so you can decide."

Follow-up drills:
When someone comes in with wrong expectations from another practice, how do you handle it? Have you tried paid ads — what happened? If Ageless were a concern for you, what would it be?
Track D
Channel partner / consultant / influencer
Signal:
They're not a practice owner. They consult for practices, run an agency, host events, or have an influencer/educator brand. Natasha is this archetype.

Opener:
Acknowledge the different role early.

"I want to make sure I'm not running a standard demo at you — you work with practices, not as one. Walk me through what you do for your clients and what would make this conversation valuable for you."

Then
STOP.
Let them teach you their business model.
CRITICAL:
If this call surfaces a real channel partnership opportunity — speaking at an event, co-presenting, a referral volume commitment —
escalate to VP Sales.
This is not a standard close path. It's a partnership conversation and the standard $499 pitch is the wrong frame.
Track E
Pre-sold warm inbound
Signal:
They mention a specific advisory board member (Nassif, Barbarino, Rajani, Shino, McKenna) as the reason they're on the call. Or they mention seeing Ageless at a specific event. The warmth is doing the work for you.

Opener:
Ask how they got here. Let them tell the origin story.

"I saw you have a meeting with us for Ageless — how'd you hear about it?"

Why it works:
They're going to tell you they saw it at AmSpa, or they follow Dr. Barbarino, or a friend recommended us. The origin story IS the first trust-building moment. Then confirm and thank them and compress discovery. Don't waste warm-inbound warmth on generic discovery.
Shorten the call.
A warm inbound should be 20–30 minutes, not 60. You don't need to convince them — you need to answer their questions and set up the close.
The 5 drill moves — use on every call regardless of archetype
Drill 1
"Who's doing that?"
When the prospect describes a process ("we run ads," "we follow up with leads," "we book consults"), ask who specifically is doing it. Agency? In-house? Front desk? Owner? Spouse? Trained on lead handling or whoever's available?

Why it matters:
You need to know who the lead handler is because that's the person whose job will change when Ageless goes live. Owner-doing-everything signals something different than a dedicated lead rep.
Drill 2
"How does that work, mechanically?"
When the prospect describes an acquisition flow ("we do meta ads," "they find us on Google," "word of mouth"), ask for the specific mechanics.

•
Meta ads — who's running them? What's your current CPL?

•
Word of mouth — when someone's referred, what's the first thing they do? Call, book online, walk in?

•
Google SEO — paid or organic? What's the primary search term people find you on?

Why it matters:
"We do meta ads" is the answer. "We paid an agency $2K/mo for 3 months, got Groupon patients, canceled" is the real story. The mechanics are where the pain lives.
Drill 3
"What happened when you tried that?"
If the prospect mentions they've tried something (marketing tool, agency, acquisition approach, another platform), ask what happened.

•
You said you tried an agency — what happened? How long did you run it?

•
You looked at Aura/Vectra/TouchMD — what made you decide against it?

•
Last open house — how did it go? How many leads did you get from it?

Why it matters:
Pain history is the cleanest path to Ageless's value prop. Yaman's agency story (3 months, Groupon patients, terminated) is worth more than 20 minutes of generic pitch.
Drill 4
"What's next on your roadmap over the next 90 days?" — most overlooked question
Ask this on every call. Every call.

Why it matters:
Catches capital priority conflicts before you've invested 25 minutes pitching. If they're mid-CRM migration, opening a new location, hiring a new provider, or launching a new service line, that changes the shape of the close. A practice opening in 45 days is a sign-up-and-pause setup. A practice finishing a CRM migration in 60 days means sequencing Ageless after the migration.

If Jennifer Milan had been asked this at minute 3, the deal doesn't go sideways at minute 24. It gets structured around the CRM timeline from the start.
Drill 5
Follow the thread
When the prospect volunteers something specific or interesting,
drill before moving on.
Don't collect and file. Collect and ask the next question.

• "We're shifting to lifestyle medicine" →
"What does that mean for your patient mix? What changes?"

• "We just terminated our agency" →
"What were they doing? What made you end it?"

• "We have VISIA in practice" →
"How do you use it in consults? What's working and not working with it?"

• "My partner is a pro bodybuilder" →
"How did the business start? Who's your patient base today?"

This is where the best calls get their gold. The prospect is telling you things, and the quality of your call is proportional to how specifically you listen.
Four techniques that matter
Technique
Validate before you reframe
When the prospect raises a concern, names a mistake, or pushes back — the first move is validation. Then you reframe.

• Yaman's bad meta ads → "That's actually a good idea in the abstract. The execution was just off"

• Jen Platinum's beta glitches question → "That's a sharp question. We've had beta clients for 6 months — we picked the hardball people"

• Shawn's control-of-consult concern → "You're thinking about it the right way. Here's why it's actually the opposite"

Pattern:
"That's a fair concern / good idea / sharp question / right instinct."
Then pivot. Never skip the validation — it's the permission to pivot.
Technique
Speak the pain back in fresh language
When you've understood the pain, describe it back in a memorable phrase. Not a summary — a reframe.

•
"You stuck your hand in the meta fan"
(Yaman's agency experience)

•
"The alternative is invisibility"
(Shawn's control-of-consult concern)

•
"We picked the hardball people"
(Jen Platinum's beta tester question)

•
"You're not losing to the practice down the street — you're losing to uncertainty"
(standard Ageless framing)

Why it matters:
A memorable phrase gives the prospect something to repeat in their head. It proves you listened. Don't force this — it comes from actually hearing what they said.
Technique
Disclose as a peer, not as an authority
When you mention your background, mention it conversationally.

Good:

•
"I worked at a booking platform for salons and spas for a few years — I know the Scottsdale area really well from that."

•
"My wife runs CS at Patient Now. She's told me about this same crossover."

•
"I've been doing this 25 years mostly with small business owners. That's probably why I notice these patterns."

Bad:

• "I'm a senior executive with 25 years of experience and I'm telling you..."

• "I've sold into thousands of practices and what I'm seeing is..."

Peer disclosures open doors. Authority drops close them.
Technique
The third-degree callout
If you've been drilling hard for 10+ minutes, it's fine — good, actually — to name it.

"I know I'm giving you the third degree here. I just want to make sure when we show you the product I'm showing you the right parts."

This is permission-in-retrospect. The prospect appreciates the transparency and it gives you license to have asked.
Bridge to demo when their story is done, not when your list is done
Cue to bridge:
They've told you about their acquisition, team, decision process, and roadmap. They've volunteered a recent pain point. They've asked a product-specific question. They've said something like "so what does this actually do?" or "so how does it work?"

Bridge script:

"OK that's really helpful. Let me show you what this looks like and we can talk specifically about how it fits your [concern they named]."

Notice: the bridge references something they told you. It proves discovery wasn't a waste of their time.
Matt's demo flow, preserved, with small additions for prospect-specific configuration. The demo itself is the proven piece — every rep who executes it cleanly gets engagement. What separates good demos from bad ones is the 30 seconds BEFORE you share the screen: configuring the demo to match the prospect, and the comprehension check midway through.
Before you share the screen — 30-second config check
Critical
Think before you click
• Do they offer wellness? If not, skip the wellness portions. Don't confuse them with services they don't have.

• Are they in Canada? Peptides like BPC-157 and tesamorelin are restricted. Don't lead with those in the wellness flow.

• Do they already own VISIA or another imaging device? Lead with
complementary
positioning, not replacement.

• Is it a values-forward operator? Pre-empt the beauty score — "this is toggleable."

• Did they say something specific in discovery you want to reference during the demo? Note it.
This is 30 seconds of thought. It prevents the peptides-to-Canadians problem (Alex/Jen Platinum) and the beauty-score-to-values-forward-MD problem (Becky/Mina/Yaman).
The website entry — show Gard first
Open the Gard Wellness example tab before the patient flow. Show the
"see your results first"
link on their homepage. This establishes: (1) what the deployment looks like on the prospect's own future website, (2) that a real customer is running this already, (3) the entry hook before the patient experience.

Then click into the Amora demo.
The patient flow
Walk through the intake. Branding is white-labeled. Questions: aesthetic treatment history, age, concerns (
"this is gold for you — you're getting intent data before she ever walks in"
), concerns map to THEIR menu only, pick a desired look. If they offer wellness, show the wellness path. If not, skip it. Photo upload — front portrait only, smartphone only. Lead capture — name, email, phone.
The analysis — don't leave dead air
While the imaging loads, narrate what's happening.
"So now the AI is doing its work — preparing her transformation image AND running the full analysis on her photo."
Dead air kills the moment.
Beauty score reveal
If pre-empted in discovery (values-forward operator):
"Remember I said this is toggleable — this is what shows if it's on. Most practices leave it on because patients engage with it like a viral moment, but your call."

If not pre-empted:
"Here's her Beauty Score — X out of 100, potential for Y. Skin age tells her she's aging slightly ahead."

Walk through strengths, "room to glow," and the upper/mid/lower face breakdown.
Before/after reveal
Slide the image back and forth.
"And notice the imaging is informed by what she told us earlier — not a generic image. She can adjust intensity, swap treatments on/off, and tinker until it feels right."

Show the CTA to book.
Comprehension check — pause here
Required
Stop talking and ask a question
At this point you've been talking for 5–7 minutes.
Pause. Ask:

"What's your reaction to this so far? Does it match what you'd want the patient experience to feel like?"

Then stop talking. Wait for the answer. Don't fill silence. The answer tells you whether the demo is landing.
Aging flow
"Now here's where we create urgency. 15 years without intervention, and 15 years with proper care."

Toggle.
This section will get a visceral reaction almost every time.
Wait for the laugh, the "oh my god," or the "I look like my mom." That reaction is the moment to ask the close question.

"Bet you've had this conversation with patients dozens of times. Now imagine them seeing it before they ever walk in."
Wellness / body flow
If they offer wellness, walk through the Tommy demo. Same pattern — emotional hook, before/after reveal, call to action.

If Canadian:
skip peptide-heavy recommendations. Stay on GLP-1s, hormone optimization.

If they don't offer wellness at all:
skip this section entirely. Don't confuse them.
Matt's flow preserved. The dashboard, star rating, enrichment, messaging, and CRM integration walkthrough that consistently lands. The AI enrichment surface in particular generates surprise-reaction moments that become buying signals.
The dashboard
Walk through the home page: potential pipeline (estimated lifetime value), consults requested, lead volume by source, top patient concerns aggregated.
The star rating
Show a 5-star lead and a 2–3 star lead. Explain the scoring: buying intent signals, number of treatments of interest, answers to the existing-patient question, AI enrichment layer.
Lead enrichment — where it gets powerful
Click into a contact card. Show what's available: before/after images, listed concerns and goals, beauty score and future self, and the
proprietary enrichment layer
— age, income bracket, net worth estimate, education, marital status, homeownership.
Prospect reaction you should expect:
surprise. Sometimes "that's creepy" (Yaman). This is fine — affirm:
"It's all public domain — we're pulling from the same data brokers your bank uses. Nothing private."
Karthik asked "is this a real person?" — that level of surprise is a buying signal.

• Manual — rep does all follow-up

• Hybrid — manual for 4–5 star leads, automated for 2–3 star

Waitlist context — your leverage
"We launched Ageless three weeks ago. We've had unprecedented demand — over a thousand practices signed up. We're being responsible with the rollout and there's a waitlist running 6–8 weeks right now for new signups."

Pause. Let this land.
The waitlist is leverage
— it's the honest answer to "can you discount" and it makes the founders club offer feel meaningful.
The founders club offer, sign-up-and-pause as required equipment, card on call as the gold standard, and reciprocal follow-up as the backup. Sign-up-and-pause is the single most important close lever we have and the most commonly missed — deploy it every time timing is the blocker.
The founders club offer
"One thing I want to extend — we ran a special at the AmSpa medical show and we're keeping it open for this conversation. Sign up before end of the month at the $499 starter — you get unlimited patients for your first month, you skip the waitlist and go live in ~48 hours, you're in the private WhatsApp community with the advisory board and the exec team, you get monthly advisory sessions with Dr. Nassif, Dr. Rajani, and the rest — and you get the founders hoodie."

Pause. Let them react.
🔑 Sign-up-and-pause — REQUIRED when timing is the blocker
Required
The single most commonly missed close move
Trigger language — deploy this if the prospect says ANY of:

• "We're not quite ready yet"

• "We're opening in [X weeks]"

• "I want to talk to my team first"

• "We're mid-[CRM migration / website redesign / build-out / hiring]"

• "We've got an event in [X] and want to time this to that"

• "The timing's tough — we just spent on [other investment]"

• Capital constraint, timing pressure, partner-needs-to-agree, sequencing concern

The script — exactly this:

"Here's an option — I can lock your $499 founders pricing today, activation starts [their specific date]. That way the timing doesn't cost you the deal terms. Want to do that?"

Then stop talking. Don't fill the silence. Wait for them to answer.
Why this works:

• Removes the deadline pressure (founders pricing expiring but their activation isn't)

• Respects their stated timing

• Converts a "maybe later" into a soft close

• They don't pay through ramp-up — they pay when they're live

• Whatever they say next is useful data — yes, or a specific new blocker

Documented successful uses:

• Carrie (Epanouir) — website redesign delay, weeks out — Stefanie locked pricing

• Karthik (Purple Basil) — wife-is-operator, 1 week ramp — Alex locked on call

• Jen Roy (Platinum) — Saturday event deadline, JT CTO expedite (opposite direction same lever)

• John (FTC Utah) — opens in 30–45 days — textbook fit that got missed. Don't miss the next one.
The standard close
If the prospect is warm and ready:

"OK — want to get you set up? I'll send the form and we can take care of it live right now — takes about 60 seconds."

Card on call is the gold standard.
Tomorrow is a deal you can lose; now is a deal you've closed.
Reciprocal follow-up — if they can't close live
"Sounds like you want to talk to [team/partner/spouse]. Here's what I'll do — I'll send you the recording from today and a summary email. If I don't hear from you by [day], I'll reach out [day after]. Sound good?"

Safety net prevents ghosting. Make it mutual.
Talk ratio reality check
Prospects who talk 30–50% of the time in the first 10 minutes close more often than prospects who talk under 20%.

If you catch yourself talking for 5+ minutes without a prospect question or response, stop. Ask a question.
Even mid-sentence.

Good mid-stream question options:

•
"What's your reaction to this so far?"

•
"Does this match what you're seeing in your practice?"

•
"Where does this land for you?"

•
"Am I on the right track here?"

Then silence. Let them answer.
The 6 objections that come up on nearly every call, with the sharp answer for each. For competitor-specific objections (Aura, VISIA, Vectra, Perfect Corp, EntityMed, Galderma, TouchMD, RxPhoto, Qoves, Aesthetics Pro, Podium, RealSelf, Facetune, InstaSize), reference the
Battle Cards tab
— those are kept current there and not duplicated here.
1. Under-promise / over-deliver — "Are patients going to feel let down?"
Common
Expectation alignment, not expectation setting
Who raises this:
Values-forward MD-led / NP-led practices, experienced injectors, anyone whose brand is built on honest results.

The weak answer:
"Well, we have a disclaimer at the bottom that says AI simulation, not a guarantee of results."
Satisfies nobody who actually cares about the values question.

The sharp answer:

"The patient already has an imagined version of the result in her head before she walks in — she's seen other people's befores and afters on your Instagram, she's compared herself to images online. Ageless makes that invisible image VISIBLE and DOCUMENTED so you can calibrate it in conversation — that's expectation alignment, not expectation setting. Your under-promise philosophy stays intact, you just get the patient's mental picture on the table instead of having to guess at it."

This protects their philosophy instead of threatening it.
2. Beauty score pushback — "That feels insulting to patients"
Common
Pre-empt, don't react
Who raises this:
Values-forward operators, anyone focused on empowerment / celebration of self / body-positive messaging.

The answer:

"Totally toggleable. Some practices love it for the viral moment — patients share their score with friends and it drives organic volume. Some turn it off because it doesn't match their brand. Your call — I'll show you both so you can see."

Bonus:
pre-empt this in discovery BEFORE they raise it if you've identified the archetype. Stops the objection from ever becoming one.
3. RMD bad reviews — "I saw negative reviews about RepeatMD"
Common
Acknowledge, own, pivot to no-contract — Alex's pattern
Who raises this:
Anyone who researched RMD before the call.

The pattern that works (Alex converted this twice in one day):

"Yeah — we had contract issues. Our contracts were 24 and 36 months and that was too long. We heard the feedback, we learned, and Ageless is different — no contract at all, month-to-month, cancel anytime."

Key:
acknowledge specifically, own it in first person, pivot to the structural fix. Don't defend. Don't deflect.
4. Pricing negotiability — "Can you discount / do better on pricing?"
Common
Hold the line. The waitlist is your leverage.
"We've got a waitlist right now — 6 to 8 weeks. We're not discounting. The founders club offer IS the concession — that's unlimited first month, skip the line, and everything else. Fair?"

"Fair" at the end is a soft commitment ask. They'll nod or explain further. Either way you've held pricing.
5. Team buy-in timing — "I want to run this by my [partner / injector / esthetician]"
Sign-up-and-pause setup
Deploy the lever
"Totally get it. Here's an option — lock founders pricing today, activation starts after your team meeting. That way the team review doesn't cost you the deal. Want to do that?"

Backup if they say no:
offer the Gong recording so the team can pre-watch at 2x.
"I can send the recording so your team can watch at 2x and come in with focused questions — that way your follow-up call is 20 minutes instead of 50."
6. Capital priority / "Not ready" — "We're too new / too small / too stretched"
Sign-up-and-pause setup
Deploy the lever — don't repeat the original offer
"Hear you. Option — lock founders pricing today, activation starts when you're ready. You don't pay through ramp-up, you don't lose founders pricing to timing. Want to do that?"

Critical:
don't repeat the offer you already gave. Restructure it. If they say "too expensive right now," don't say "but it's only $499" — say "lock pricing, activate later."

Field-proven questions — surfaced across 13 live calls
These questions emerged from analyzing real demo calls. Each one consistently unlocked better discovery than standard funnel questions. Use them across all verticals before going into the problem-area sequences above.
Funnel leak locator — best discovery question in the dataset
"Where do you feel like the biggest disconnect is — from ad to booking, from booking to showing up, or from showing up to converting?"
Forces the prospect to self-identify exactly where they're leaking rather than just describing their traffic sources. The answer tells you which Ageless capability to lead with. A prospect who says "ad to booking" needs the visualization and lead quality story. One who says "showing up to converting" needs the pre-sold patient and consultation efficiency angle. One who says "booking to showing up" has a commitment problem — the Future Aging Self is your entry point.
Practice structure — ask this early, it changes everything
"Is it just you at the practice, or do you have staff handling inbound and follow-up?"
Solo vs. staffed is a fundamental fork in how you pitch. A solo operator can't run a disciplined lead follow-up cadence — for them, automation is the entire value proposition, not a nice-to-have. A staffed practice has a delegation problem. Ask this in the first three minutes. Learning it at minute 21 means you've been pitching the wrong angle the whole call.
Capacity and urgency check
"Are you at a place where you're really looking to fill the schedule, or are you pretty full right now?"
Reveals urgency, growth stage, and which use case to lead with. Open capacity → acquisition story. Full schedule → cross-sell and reactivation. Also surfaces new provider or new location situations where there's sudden capacity and genuine urgency.
Failed marketing excavation — don't skip it
"You mentioned you've tried marketing before — what happened when you followed up with those leads? What was the response like?"
When a prospect says marketing hasn't worked, most reps move on. Don't. The failure story is the setup for Ageless's entire positioning. Dig in: What kind of ads? What was the call-to-action? What did people say when you called? The answer almost always reveals promotion-anchored traffic that brought price-shoppers — which sets up the curiosity-anchored vs. discount-anchored reframe perfectly.
Decision-maker check — confirm before investing 40 minutes
"Will the person who makes the final call on something like this be on today, or will you be presenting this to someone afterward?"
Two of six calls in the dataset had the decision-maker not in the room. In both cases the deal went to a follow-up without the rep present. Ask this at the very start. If the decision-maker isn't on, restructure toward "here's what you need to present" and make sure your post-call email goes directly to the decision-maker, not just through the proxy.
For existing RepeatMD customers — ask this before anything else
"How are you currently using RepeatMD and what's working well for you?"
Six calls in the dataset involved current or paused RepeatMD customers — Matt, Stephanie, Joyce, Jamey, Elliot, Dwayne — and a clear pattern has emerged. Every single one was either underutilizing the platform, paused, or actively frustrated with some aspect of RMD. Joyce's practice was only using Affirm financing. Stephanie had a months-long Canadian tax billing problem. Dwayne's account was paused during a build-out. Elliot's was paused entirely. Matt discovered Ageless through the admin portal and only used RMD lightly.

Asking this question early does three things: (1) it surfaces the underutilization problem so you can give them a quick activation win (staff language, QR code placement, gift card promos) that builds trust before you pitch anything new; (2) it sets up Ageless as the thing that makes the investment they're already making worthwhile — "you've got the retention engine, Ageless is what fills it with the right patients in the first place"; (3) it flags any open RMD issues that need to be routed to CS before you can close — trying to upsell on top of a live billing complaint reads as tone-deaf and kills the deal.

For RMD-paused prospects specifically:
follow up with "What would need to be true for you to unpause RepeatMD alongside this?" This gives you the account's actual needs and flags whether they're a candidate for the combined retention + acquisition play once Ageless proves out. Don't skip this on any existing or former RMD customer call. The churn risk you defuse becomes the trust that closes the upsell.

Pricing & Commitment
5 objections — cost, contracts, ROI, trial requests, down market
▶
"It's too expensive."
▶
You pay $7-10 per patient visualized. When that patient closes, they're worth $3,000-$5,000 in revenue. If Ageless helps close just two extra patients per month, the subscription pays for itself many times over. And the first month is $499 with unlimited patients — real volume, real test, no cap, no risk of running out of room to prove it.

For prospects who want to run their own numbers:
ageless-gain-calculator.lovable.app
lets them plug in conservative conversion rates and still see the math work at their specific price point and visit frequency.
"I need to see ROI before committing."
▶
That's exactly what the first month is designed for. At $499 with unlimited patients, you have everything you need to put it to a real test. If Ageless doesn't prove itself in 30 days with real leads and real bookings, you can walk away. No contract, no risk, no artificial cap limiting how much you can actually test.

If the prospect wants to model it before committing, send the interactive calculator:
ageless-gain-calculator.lovable.app
— they can plug in their own conversion rate, average visit value, and return frequency. Use it as a tool to surface their specific numbers, not as a promise.
"Do you have a trial period or discount to get started?"
▶
The unlimited first month at $499 is the trial — and it's better than a week-long free trial because you're seeing it work with your real patient base, not a sandboxed environment. You'll know within two weeks if it's driving bookings. If it's not, you cancel. No contract, no call required, cancel right in the product.
"We tried something like this before."
▶
Was it scoring your leads by income and intent? Was it auto-enrolling patients in a rewards program with a welcome credit? Was it showing Affirm financing alongside the visualization? Was it sending AI-powered text and email follow-up automatically? Ageless is a full qualification engine. Whatever you tried before almost certainly wasn't doing all of that in one place.
"Patients aren't spending like they used to — the economy is tough right now."
▶
This is a real and increasingly common read, and it's worth taking seriously — because the macro story genuinely looks rough. Credit card debt is at an all-time high north of $1.2 trillion. January was the worst month for job cuts since 2009. Oil is surging on Iran tensions. The easy money era is over, and public aesthetics companies are getting crushed — Beauty Health is down nearly 90% over five years. Private equity is rolling up medspa platforms because the independent operators are squeezed.

So you'd think nobody's spending on aesthetics and wellness. You'd be wrong.

40M
Americans on GLP-1s
brand-new patient category
$15B+
aesthetic market size
at all-time highs
2×
demand growth
since pre-COVID baseline
Demand in this category has never been higher. GLP-1s alone created a brand-new patient segment of forty million Americans who didn't exist as buyers two years ago. The aesthetic market is at all-time highs. Consumer demand has doubled since pre-COVID. The money hasn't disappeared — it's shifted.

Your patient who used to spend $600 a visit on luxury skincare is now spending $800 a month on a GLP-1 program and asking you about the filler she saw on Instagram. She didn't stop spending on looking and feeling younger. She reallocated. The practices that are struggling right now aren't losing to a bad economy — they're losing to the practices that adapted faster to where the demand actually is.

That's what Ageless is built for. In a market where every patient has more places to spend their money, the practice that closes the patient in front of them wins. Ageless makes sure every visitor to your site, every lead from your ads, every follower in your Instagram bio turns into a scored, pre-sold, ready-to-book patient. In a down market you can't afford to waste a single lead. That's the argument
for
this tool, not against it.

Product & Results
5 objections — AI accuracy, comparisons, visualization realism, patient reactions
▶
"I don't like the beauty score — that feels harsh to my patients."
▶
This one comes up often enough that it's worth leading with rather than waiting for the objection — especially for operators with a patient-empowerment brand voice. The answer is simple: the score is optional. You turn it off in settings, and the rest of the flow runs exactly the same. Becky (TOPS Medical Spa) and Mina (Lamb Medical) both preferred it off, and both closed once they knew.

The framing that lands fastest: "If your brand is 'we work with you on what you want, not what we think you need,' turn the score off — a lot of practices with your brand position do exactly that. The visualization, the AI recommendations, the full flow all still work. The score is the one piece that's values-dependent, so we made it configurable."

That validates the prospect's values before giving the feature answer, which closes the loop faster than defending the score.
"How accurate are the visualizations?"
▶
They're clinically informed previews validated by our Medical Advisory Board — including Dr. Paul Nassif from Botched, Dr. Anil Rajani who's a Top 10 injector in America, and Dr. Shino Bay, the #1 Sculptra provider in the US. These are not beauty filters. The AI is trained on treatment data and reviewed by clinicians. We use the word "visualization" and "preview," not "results," because these are possibilities, not guarantees.
"I'm worried the AI visualization sets expectations better than what I can actually deliver."
▶
That's the sharpest version of this concern and the one that comes up on every clinician call — Brette, Wenzel, Elliot. The instinctive answer is to lead with credibility (advisory board, 15 physicians, "visualization not results" language) and all of that is true and worth saying. But it misses the actual reframe that converts this objection.

The reframe — especially sharp for MD-led practices on the "under promise, over deliver" philosophy (Mina, Laura, Wenzel, Jennifer Milan):
You're already having this conversation. Every patient who walks into your consultation arrives with a mental image of what they want. You just can't see it. You're managing expectations against an invisible target — which is the hardest version of the problem. Ageless doesn't introduce an expectation where none existed. It makes the patient's existing expectation visible, shared, and documented before they ever sit in your chair.

For physicians committed to clinical honesty, this is the protection, not the threat: the under-promise philosophy works best when you know what the patient is expecting. Right now they arrive with a private, undocumented expectation; with Ageless they arrive with a shared, consent-documented one, and your consultation becomes about calibrating a known image rather than guessing at an invisible one. Your clinical integrity is preserved — the AI is the conversation starter, you remain the authority who shapes the treatment plan.

That's the flip. Right now you're the only one in the room who can't see what the patient is picturing. With Ageless, you and the patient are looking at the same image, and
you
are the authority in the conversation about what's clinically achievable versus what the visualization shows. The consultation shifts from convincing a skeptical patient that something is possible to managing the enthusiasm of a patient who's already bought in. You go from defense to offense.

On the compliance layer specifically: the advisory board wrote the disclaimer and "visualization / preview, not results" language specifically to protect clinical practices. Three consent checkboxes before any imaging. The patient has acknowledged it's a visualization, not a guarantee, before they see anything. Most surgeons tell us this actually reduces their liability exposure compared to the status quo where patients arrive with undocumented expectations in their head.
"What's the difference between this and Facetune, or tools I already use to show results?"
▶
The honest answer is the image itself isn't the whole point — it's what happens around it. Facetune, ChatGPT, Gemini — a patient can probably produce some version of a before-and-after on their own. But here's what they can't do: get a visualization trained on hundreds of thousands of clinical before-and-afters, reviewed by a board of 15 physicians for realistic outcomes, in a way that also captures their contact info, scores their intent, enriches their profile with income data, and automatically follows up based on exactly what they explored. Facetune gives them a selfie. Ageless gives you a lead.
"What if patients don't like what they see?"
▶
That's actually a feature, not a bug. A patient who sees the visualization and decides it's not for them was never going to book anyway. They would have wasted your staff's time in a 45-minute consultation. Ageless filters them out before they cost you that time.
"Can I try it on my own face before committing?"
▶
Yes — and we encourage it. The most common path is we can walk you through it right now on this call. Pull up your camera, take a front-facing photo and a side profile, and we'll run you through the full patient experience live. You'll get your beauty score, see your before-and-after, and experience the Future Aging Self. Most people who do it on themselves stop asking questions and start asking how to sign up.

If we can't do it live, we'll send you a link after — but experiencing it on a demo photo is genuinely different from experiencing it on your own face. The emotional response is the whole product.
📅
Fit & Timing
4 objections — wrong patients, staff capacity, integrations, readiness
▶
"Is Ageless included in my RepeatMD subscription?"
▶
It's a separate product and a separate bill — $499 a month, no contract, cancels right inside the product, no call required. It integrates with your RepeatMD dashboard so you see everything in one place, and if you have Affirm through RepeatMD the welcome offer and financing can surface inside the Ageless flow too. Think of it as the acquisition layer that feeds the retention engine you already have. You built the system for keeping patients — Ageless is what fills it with the right ones in the first place.
"Would your texting come from my existing office number or a new generated one?"
▶
It's a separate Twilio marketing number — same setup as RepeatMD's outreach. Most practices handle it one of two ways: they use the Twilio number for automated follow-up texts and keep their own phone for inbound calls, or they turn off the auto-texting entirely and just do manual outreach from the platform. Either works. The goal is making sure no automated message goes out from a number that patients might try to call back expecting to reach the front desk — so whichever way you set it up, just make sure your team knows which number is which.
"We already get enough leads."
▶
You don't have a lead problem. You have a conversion problem. How many of those leads show up ready to buy? Ageless doesn't replace your lead gen — it upgrades the quality. Patients arrive pre-visualized and pre-committed. Your staff spends less time convincing and more time confirming.
"We tried marketing before and it just brought the wrong patients — cheap, not our demographic."
▶
That experience is more common than you'd think, and the root cause is almost always the same: the marketing was anchored to a promotion or a discount. When the first thing a patient sees is a price offer, that becomes the anchor for the entire relationship. They book for the deal, they don't rebook at full price, and your calendar fills with the wrong people.

Ageless is anchored to curiosity, not discounts. A patient sees your ad, clicks through, uploads their selfie, and sees what their face looks like with your treatments. By the time they contact you, they're not asking what your Botox costs — they're asking when they can come in. The anchor is "I want to look like that," not "I want the cheapest deal." That's a completely different patient walking through your door.
"My staff is already overwhelmed with follow-up."
▶
That's exactly the problem Ageless solves. The intelligent outreach layer follows up automatically via text and email the moment a patient completes their visualization — personalized to the specific treatments they explored, running 24/7 without any staff involvement. Your team doesn't add to their workload. They handle the patients who are already warmed up and ready to book.
"Our leads just aren't converting."
▶
Three reasons leads don't convert: they're not qualified, they're not emotionally committed, and nobody followed up fast enough. Ageless fixes all three. The AI visualization creates commitment before the consult. The 1-5 star scoring with income and job data tells your team who to call first. And intelligent outreach follows up automatically via text and email within minutes, not days. No more leads going cold because someone forgot to call back.
🤝
Trust & Credibility
4 objections — proof, AI skepticism, patient concerns, exclusivity
▶
"Do you sell this to practices within 10 or 15 miles of us? Is there market exclusivity?"
▶
Two-layer honest answer.
Layer one:
The tool is fully white-labeled to your practice — your logo, your colors, your link, your branded flow. Your patient experience is yours, not Ageless's. A competitor using the same underlying tool in your market would still be a completely different product from the patient's perspective because the branding, the service menu recommendations, the consultation language, and the lead capture all live under your brand.

Layer two:
There is a real first-mover advantage we're not shy about. The first practice in a local market to deploy Ageless creates the patient expectation that this is how aesthetic consultations work. Every competitor who adopts Ageless after you is chasing that expectation — they're not the ones who defined it. That first-mover window matters specifically in markets where competition is tight, and the founders club pricing with same-week onboarding exists to let you claim that position before your competitors do.

We don't sell exclusivity contracts. We give you the tools to be the practice that made the tool matter in your market.
"What are your conversion rates? Can you prove this works?"
▶
We've been live for about a month, so our dataset is still growing — but the early results are strong. One practice sent their Ageless link to 100 existing patients in a single email. Twelve went through the full visualization. Seven of them booked treatments for services they'd never tried at that practice before — off one email. Another practice generated over $10,000 in same-day revenue from a single event where patients were passing phones around comparing beauty scores. And a third saw $7,500 in high-ticket bookings (Ulthera + injectables) from one consultation that started with the visualization.

We're early and we're honest about that. But the conversion rates we're seeing are substantially higher than a standard contact form or Facebook lead ad — and the lead quality difference is the reason why. You're not comparing apples to apples.
"Patients don't want AI telling them what to do."
▶
Ageless doesn't tell them what to do. It shows them what's possible on their own face. They explore at their own pace, privately, with no pressure. By the time they reach you, they've already decided. That's not AI pressure. That's AI-assisted clarity.
"I'm not sure AI is right for our practice."
▶
That's a fair instinct and worth examining. What specifically concerns you — the accuracy, the patient experience, the brand fit, or something else? The practices that have been hesitant for brand reasons usually find that the product's premium look and feel actually elevates the brand perception rather than cheapening it. The ones hesitant about accuracy come around quickly once they see the advisory board credentials and run it on their own face. What's driving the hesitation for you?
Continuation
Second calls, multi-touch deals, and the work between conversations — where most Ageless deals are actually won or lost
Ageless sits in a category with more decision-makers than most vertical SaaS. A medspa, plastic surgery, or wellness practice buying a patient acquisition tool often involves a marketing agency, a partner physician, a spouse, or an office manager — any of whom may or may not be in the room on the first call.
When the room is complete and the decision-maker is present, close in the room.
When the buying committee extends beyond the call, the second conversation is where the deal is actually worked — and running it with the same intention as the first is what separates reps who carry those deals to close from reps who lose them to silence. This section is the playbook for the multi-stakeholder version of the deal.
🧭
Diagnose the Deal State
Before you plan the second call, know which kind of deal you're looking at — the plays are different for each
Live & Locked
Card on file or hard commit
Verbal close with a confirmed follow-up time, named attendees, and a clear activation path. The deal is won — the second call is implementation, not selling.
RegenRx, Living Waters, Keraderm, Blessed Beauty, Regenerative & Restorative
Live but Parked
Genuine timing constraint
Real external blocker — EMR transition, website revamp, hiring disruption. The prospect wants to move forward but can't yet. Parking is fine. Parking without a mechanism is how deals die.
Skin Serenity (Boulevard), Isabella (hiring), Myleen (website)
Alive but Exposed
Verbal interest, soft follow-up
Decision-maker not in the room, no card taken, follow-up scheduled but conditioned on a stakeholder you haven't met. These are the deals where second-call execution decides the outcome.
Craig (marketing team gate), Mari (partner not present), Linda (Ella reference pending)
The move:
At the end of every first call, label the deal in one of these three states before you close the laptop. If you can't, you didn't close the first call tightly enough — and the second call will inherit that ambiguity.
🎯
Running the Second Call
Three frameworks that reliably advance a deal — not just continue it
The Re-Open — set the outcome before they do
Don't open with "great to see you again." Open with the ask.
"I want to make sure this call is worth both your time and [new person]'s. What's the outcome that would make this a productive 30 minutes for you?"
This is a lock-the-call move at the start instead of at the end. It works better because the prospect hasn't yet spent political capital saying "I'm not buying." You're getting their definition of success on the record before the conversation starts — which means you now know what you're aiming at, and they've committed to it out loud.

Read the answer:

- If the new person answers — you know who's really running the decision.
- If your original champion answers — the new person is along for the ride, which is a different sale.
- If nobody answers clearly — you're not going to close this call and you should adjust expectations immediately.

The Translation Gap — recover the pitch your champion mangled
Between call one and call two, your champion has had a conversation about you without you. They translated your pitch — usually badly.
"What did you tell [partner/marketing person] about this after our first call? I want to make sure I reinforce what resonated and clean up anything that didn't land."
This surfaces the translation gap instantly. You'll almost always hear a version of your pitch that's missing the one thing that would have closed it. Your job in the next ten minutes is to put that thing back in the room, in front of the person who didn't hear it the first time.

Follow-up if the answer is thin: "What questions did they have that you couldn't fully answer because I wasn't there?" That's the objection you're handling on this call, whether it gets surfaced otherwise or not.

The Proxy Interview — when the DM still isn't in the room
If you run a second call and the decision-maker isn't there, stop pitching. Extract.
Ask these in sequence, pausing on each. You're using the gatekeeper as a research tool, not trying to close them.

- "If [DM name] were on this call right now, what's the first question they'd ask?"
- "What are they worried about that you think they wouldn't say out loud?"
- "What would make them say yes on the spot versus want to think about it?"
- "What's the last tool like this they said no to, and why?"

End the call with the ask: "Based on what you just told me, I'd like fifteen minutes directly with [DM]. Can you set that up this week?" That's the close. Not another group meeting — a direct line.

Why this works:
The gatekeeper can't close. Treating them like they can is how Skin Serenity-type deals stall indefinitely. Use them as a source of intelligence, then escalate to the person who can sign.
📡
Between Calls
The texts, emails, and touchpoints that keep a deal warm — and when to send them
Pre-Meeting Ammunition — the email your champion actually needs
Most reps send a recap after the first call. That's defense. Offense is arming the champion
before
their internal meeting.
Send a second email 24 hours before your champion's internal conversation — not 24 hours after your demo. Structure it this way:

- Name the meeting explicitly: "You're meeting with [marketing person / partner / spouse] on [day]."
- List the three questions the absent stakeholder is most likely to ask, with your answers to each (method below).
- Calibrate those three questions to the gatekeeper archetype — a marketing agency's questions are not a partner physician's questions.
- Close with: "If any of this doesn't sound right or you'd rather have me on the call, I can join with 15 minutes of notice."

That last sentence is the move. It gives your champion permission to invite you into the meeting without losing face. Roughly one in three will take you up on it. The ones who don't are now better armed than they would have been.

Generating the three questions — the method
The three questions aren't a guess. They come from the first call transcript plus what you know about the gatekeeper archetype. Pull the Gong transcript, drop it into Claude with the prompt below, and let it do the pattern-match for you. You'll get back a draft in 30 seconds — then edit for voice and accuracy.

Copy into Claude
I had a first sales call with a prospect who is evaluating Ageless AI, our patient acquisition product for medical aesthetic and wellness practices. The decision-maker was not on the call, but my champion on the call will now be presenting this internally to
[insert role: marketing agency lead / partner physician / spouse MD / office manager]
.

Based on this transcript, identify the three questions the absent stakeholder is most likely to ask when my champion describes this product to them. Focus on the stakeholder's specific concerns given their role — not generic objections. For each question, give me a 2-3 sentence answer my champion can use directly, written in their voice (not sales-y, not corporate).

Prioritize questions that:
- Came up implicitly in the call but weren't fully answered
- Are specific to this prospect's practice, stack, and situation
- The stakeholder is likely to raise because of their role, even if nobody on the call mentioned them

Transcript follows:
[paste Gong transcript here]
Then edit the output. Claude will draft — you check it against what you actually heard on the call and refine before sending to the champion.
Quality check before you send:
Read your own ammunition email as if you were the absent stakeholder. Does it read like a rep coaching a champion — or like a rep answering the stakeholder directly? It should feel like the latter. If your champion can paraphrase it in their own words and it still sounds natural, it's working. If it sounds like corporate sales copy when the champion reads it aloud, rewrite it.
The Parking Mechanism — for legitimate timing constraints
When a deal genuinely needs to pause, the parking conversation has four parts. Skip any one of them and the deal dies quietly.
- Name the specific reactivation trigger. Not "we'll follow up in a few weeks." Specific: "The day Boulevard goes live." "The Monday after your site relaunches." "The week your new hire completes training."
- Lock a specific follow-up time tied to that trigger. On the calendar, with both people, before the current call ends. Vague commitments are dead commitments.
- Give the champion community access immediately. WhatsApp founders club, peer references, whatever applies. A cold prospect in a three-week gap loses interest. A prospect who's been reading WhatsApp messages from other practices arrives warmer than they left.
- Check in mid-gap with one light touchpoint. Not a sales follow-up. Something useful — a case study relevant to their vertical, a product update, a peer in their area who just went live. One touchpoint. Don't flood them.

The Cadence — a rhythm you can actually run
A default cadence for a live-but-parked or alive-but-exposed deal. Adjust to the deal, but don't let the gap exceed the next touch.
Same day
Recap email.
Sent within two hours of the first call. Short. Three bullets on what was discussed, the offer, and the next step with a specific date. Include the WhatsApp community invite.
Day 2–3
Value touchpoint.
Something useful that isn't a sales ask — a peer case study, a product update, a link to a relevant testimonial. Keeps the relationship warm without pressure.
24h before internal meeting
Pre-meeting ammunition email.
Three likely questions, three answers, offer to join on 15 minutes notice. This is the single highest-leverage touchpoint in the cadence.
Day of second call
Morning-of text.
Short. "Looking forward to today at [time]. Anything come up I should be ready to address?" Creates a reply surface for last-minute objections before they derail the call.
Mid-gap (parked deals)
One light check-in.
Around the midpoint of the park. Not "just checking in" — give them something. A product update, a relevant win from another practice, a case study. One touchpoint only.
3 days before reactivation
Reactivation reminder.
You reach out to them, not the other way around. Half of parked deals die because nobody resurfaces them on time. Confirm the original reactivation time is still good.
🔑
Gatekeeper Archetypes
Four patterns that keep showing up — click any to expand the play
📋
The Office Manager
Operationally sharp, not financially empowered
▶
What they're actually asking
Will this disrupt my workflow. Will staff actually use it. Does it integrate with what we already run. Am I going to be the one explaining this to the team when it breaks.
The play
Speak to operational load, not ROI. Give them specific language to take to the MD: "Here's what this does for your front desk specifically." Make their life easier, not just the practice's bottom line.
What to send before the internal meeting
A short operational summary — how it integrates with their EMR and booking system, what the staff workflow looks like, what training they'd need. Skip the revenue math. That's the MD's conversation, not theirs.
Watch for
They may already be advocating for you internally — or quietly killing the deal. Ask the proxy interview questions early to figure out which.
Pattern example: Skin Serenity (Rebekah, office manager — Dr. Suponya not on call)
📣
The Marketing Person or Agency
Reads AI acquisition tools as a threat to their scope
▶
What they're actually asking
Does this replace me. Does this make my dashboard numbers look bad. Does this bypass the system I already built. Is my retainer in danger.
The play
Position as amplifier, not replacer. Ageless makes their paid media work 3-5x harder because the landing experience does the heavy lifting. Their CAC reporting looks
better
, not worse. Reframe the conversation from "new tool" to "makes your existing work perform."
What to send before the internal meeting
The landing experience section of the Acquisition Deep Dive. Show them the page-by-page conversion comparison. Let them see where Ageless fits in the funnel they already own.
Watch for
Agencies sometimes have a competing tool they're already paid to promote. Ask directly: "Are they currently running or recommending any similar tools?" Better to know before the call.
Pattern example: Craig / Westport Medispa (2pm marketing team gate on verbal close)
🩺
The Partner Physician
Clinical, skeptical of marketing claims, worried about reputational risk
▶
What they're actually asking
Is this compliant. Does it set realistic expectations. Does it feel professional enough for my brand. Am I going to get a patient showing up angry because the visualization didn't match.
The play
Lead with the 15-physician advisory board and the "visualization / preview, not results" language discipline.
Do not lead with revenue numbers.
Revenue math is for the business owner — the physician wants to know the clinical posture is sound before they'll listen to anything else.
What to send before the internal meeting
The advisory board names and credentials. Screenshots of the disclaimer language. One testimonial from a clinician-led practice, not an owner-operator. Make it easy for them to say "this isn't going to embarrass me."
Watch for
Surgical specialties especially — the liability concern is real. Acknowledge it directly, don't handwave. Remy's Dr. Wenzel call is the reference for how to run this conversation when it comes up live.
Pattern example: Mari / SkinLab (partner not in room, Friday close depends on recording review)
💍
The Spouse / MD
Variable — sometimes operationally involved, sometimes hands-off
▶
What they're actually asking
Does my partner believe in this. Is this a distraction from the real business. Are we committing to something we can't unwind. What happens to our relationship if this doesn't work.
The play
Understand through your champion what the spouse's
specific
concern is before the second call. Don't handle it generically — ask what they'd push back on, then address it by name. This is the archetype where the pre-meeting ammunition email matters most.
What to send before the internal meeting
The cancellation and commitment language — month-to-month, no contract, cancel in-product. Most spouse objections collapse when the reversibility is made concrete. Also include one peer reference from a similarly structured practice.
Watch for
Sometimes the spouse is the actual operator and the "business owner" is the title-holder. If that's the case, you're running a proxy interview — get the spouse on the next call directly.
Pattern example: Craig / Westport (wife is the MD, not on call; decision runs through her)
🧠
Reading the Room
When to close in the room, when to set up the second act — and why the distinction matters
The mindset shift
Same-day close is always the goal when the full buying committee is in the room. The nuance in this category is that the committee isn't always complete on call one — a medspa, plastic surgery, or wellness practice often has two to four stakeholders involved in a tool decision, and some of them are reached through your champion rather than directly. When that's the shape of the deal, forcing a same-day close on an incomplete room is how you break the relationship with your champion — they feel pressured, go quiet, and you lose the deal you would have won with a better second call.

When the room is complete, close it. When it isn't, run the second call as a main event — not a recovery move.

Reps who internalize this read the room more accurately on call one. They close the deals that are closeable, and they set up the multi-stakeholder deals to win on call two — instead of spending their energy fighting for a commitment the buyer can't legitimately make yet.
📊
Second-Call Scorecard
How to grade a second call — for yourself, for a peer, or for the War Room
Five checks. Score each one yes or no.
For any deal that didn't close in call one — grade the follow-up the same way you grade the first call.
- Did we identify the actual decision-maker and get them in the second call — or extract their concerns through a proper proxy interview?
- Did we surface the translation gap in the first ten minutes by asking what the champion told others about call one?
- Did we send pre-meeting ammunition before the internal conversation, not a recap after the demo?
- Did we correctly identify the gatekeeper archetype and adjust the play accordingly?
- Did we lock the third step — with a specific date, specific attendees, and a specific outcome — before ending the second call?

5 / 5 — Elite
Deal is on rails. If it doesn't close, something external happened.
3–4 / 5 — Solid
Workmanlike. Flag the miss and run the same deal type better next time.
0–2 / 5 — Gap
This is where deals die. The War Room should flag why.
🎬
Second-Call War Room
Tape analysis for continuation calls — populates as deals progress
Linda Yenokians — Upkeep Skin Clinic
· Second call
Dominique Simone (solo) · 4 min · Gap to 1st call: 2 days
● No buy — graceful decline

▸
Linda Yenokians — Upkeep Skin Clinic
· Second call

● No buy — graceful decline
▶ Gong (follow-up)
▶ First call

Pricing + Ella reference
