What happened between the two calls
Gap analysis
The thing that was supposed to close the deal is what killed it
On the first call, the single highest-value unplayed asset was Linda's colleague Ella — a peer who had just gone live with Ageless that week. The recommendation in the first-call analysis was explicit: reach Ella in the WhatsApp community before Friday, make a direct introduction, and let Ella's experience close Linda. Instead, Linda talked to Ella directly and unmediated — and learned that Ella was on a free trial. That fact alone reframed Linda's entire read on the $499 founders offer. A price that felt fair on Friday felt punitive on Monday.

Second compounding factor: Linda used the two-day gap to think more carefully about her own economics. She surfaced on this call that luminaMD skincare sales in her clinic have dropped sharply year-over-year — patients cutting discretionary spend down to cleanser + vitamin C only. In a contracting spend environment, a $500/month bet on a new acquisition tool reads differently than it did during the emotional peak of the first-call demo.
What worked on the second call
Strong
Dominique didn't argue the Ella situation — acknowledged it immediately
When Linda raised the free trial issue, Dominique explained the timing cleanly: the trial was a launch-period offer that expired, it wasn't even available at AmSpa, lots of practices were hearing about it retroactively through peers. No defensiveness, no pushback on whether Ella should have mentioned it. This was the right posture — disputing Linda's read would have damaged the relationship; validating it preserved the option of a future deal.
When a prospect surfaces information that undermines your pricing positioning, acknowledge the underlying fairness of their read before you re-frame. Dominique did this well. The rep move that fails in this situation is defending the current price aggressively — that converts a "no for now" into a "never."
Strong
Framed the tier price as "proof-of-itself" rather than a standard monthly subscription
Dominique's strongest moment on the call was reframing the $499 not as a price but as a commitment-test structure: "the tiers could be a little bit on the pricier side, but the difference between our tiers and working with an agency or consultant is it's really designed to prove itself to you — unlimited first month, no contract, walk away if it's not working." This is the right frame for an operator who has been burned by marketing spend before, which Linda has been (three failed agency attempts from the first-call analysis).
The "prove itself" framing is currently scattered across various pricing talk tracks and should be formalized. It's specifically effective against the "$499 is too much" objection because it reframes the purchase as a test, not a recurring cost. Worth a named entry in the Objections tab.
What didn't work — and where the deal actually died
Gap
The Toronto economic context landed unanswered
Linda's clearest reason for passing wasn't the price or the Ella situation — it was the macroeconomic read she articulated at 3:13: "patients are not spending as they were, we're seeing a very big decline in what patients are spending, living costs in Ontario is quite high." This is a real business condition, not a stall tactic. Dominique's response didn't engage with it — she pivoted to the relationship play ("if there ever is any promotion I'll keep you top of mind"). That's a fine tactical close, but it leaves the strategic objection unanswered.

The answer that would have re-opened the door: "If your patients are spending less on luxury skincare, they're not spending less on looking younger — that's a wellness investment, not a discretionary one. Ageless is the tool designed for exactly this market: helping you reach patients who still want the outcome when they've cut the add-ons." That reframes contraction as the problem Ageless is built to solve, not the reason to skip it.
The "economic contraction" objection is going to recur — Canada and the US are both in the same softening spend environment. A standard talk track for this objection should be built into the Objections tab. The core move: the tightening market is the argument *for* a conversion-focused tool, not against. Every dollar spent on unqualified traffic is wasted; Ageless makes each dollar work harder, which matters more in a down market, not less.
Gap
Didn't use the Continuation playbook — no re-open question, no translation-gap surface
The Continuation tab prescribes opening second calls with the question "what's the outcome that would make this a productive conversation?" Dominique opened instead with "do you have any questions you want me to run through with you again?" — a passive opener that let Linda control the frame from word one. Given Linda had already talked to Ella and made her decision, she was going to pass regardless, but the passive opener made the "no" arrive faster than a more structured re-engagement would have.

The translation-gap question — "what did you tell Ella about this after our first call?" — would also have surfaced the free-trial landmine earlier in the conversation, giving Dominique a chance to address it before Linda delivered her decision.
This is the first real test of the Continuation playbook in the dataset and it wasn't used. Worth making it the standard second-call template for Dominique and the team — opening with the outcome question and the translation-gap question, in that order, before anything else.
The broader signal — this is a win, not a loss
Relationship
Linda called specifically to decline — that's a signal, not a setback
Most prospects who decide not to buy simply go quiet. Linda didn't. She took the follow-up call specifically to tell Dominique "no" in person. Her words: "I did want to take your call and tell you that personally." That's not a prospect who's done — that's a prospect who values the relationship and is keeping the door open. The final exchange confirmed it: she asked Dominique to save her number and stay in touch about future promotions.

Three realistic paths back into this account: (1) a future founders-period discount or equivalent; (2) Ella's results, if they end up strong, become the reference Linda needed; (3) the Ontario economic softness eases. Dominique's posture preserved all three.
Lessons from the call — not a scorecard (yet)
The Continuation playbook didn't exist when this call was run. In fact, this call was part of what inspired the tab. So this isn't a scorecard against Dominique — it's a retrospective on what the tape taught us that's now baked into the framework every rep has access to going forward.
What the tape taught us about peer references:
Unmediated peer conversations can surface information that reshapes the entire deal read (Ella's free trial). The lesson — now in the playbook — is to make the introduction yourself, in the community, with context, before the prospect reaches out cold.
What the tape taught us about second-call openers:
Starting with "do you have any questions?" lets the prospect control the frame. The outcome-anchor open ("what would make this a productive conversation?") is now the standard because of calls like this one.
What the tape taught us about translation gaps:
The Ella free-trial landmine would have surfaced earlier with a translation-gap question ("what did you tell Ella about this after our first call?"). That question is now named in the playbook specifically because this deal showed its value.
What Dominique did right under real conditions:
Didn't argue the Ella situation, didn't defend the price aggressively, delivered the "prove itself" reframe cleanly, preserved the relationship for future re-engagement. On a cold second call with a decided prospect, those moves matter more than scripted plays.
The honest read:
Linda's decision was probably already made by the time this call started. The deal died when she talked to Ella unmediated, not during this four-minute conversation. The value of this tape isn't in what should have been done differently — it's that it showed us what a second-call framework needed to include. The Continuation tab exists partly because of it.

What happened between the two calls
Gap analysis
Jennifer reviewed the social proof doc — two questions emerged
Stefanie sent a sales data document after the first call that Jennifer described as "pretty good data." Jennifer surfaced a specific question on that doc at 4:32 about the phone-passing anecdote (turned out to be an open-house use case). The follow-up opened with Stefanie asking "what questions do you have for me?" — which is the right open for a warm second call where the prospect has done homework.

The real reason the second call existed: Jennifer needed to bring in Carrie (the owner), who joined at 3:04 with a specific operational concern about patient-flow friction. Carrie’s question at 8:50 is the real inflection point of this call — "what is your experience with actual patient now?" That moved the conversation from "are we going to buy this" to "how will this integrate with our existing EMR stack." Integration concerns at second-call stage almost always mean the prospect is pricing the deal internally.
What worked
Strong
Sign-up-and-pause closing lever surfaced naturally — new move for the playbook
When Jennifer mentioned the website redesign was in progress, Stefanie didn’t push for immediate activation. Instead at 7:50 she introduced what is now documented as the sign-up-and-pause close: "our founder put that in the channel, they have let people sign up for that and then pause that until you were ready to use it. So you’d sign up with that 499 price, and then we are just creating a document and giving it to onboarding saying they don’t want this released. So your month unlimited wouldn’t start until you told us that you were ready." She named two specific practices already using it — one deploying June 11, one May 11. Concrete examples make the move feel real rather than theoretical.

This is a closing lever that doesn’t exist anywhere else in the sales tool documentation and it came straight from this call. The whole Sign-up-and-pause pattern card in the War Room exists because of this tape.
This is the exact right move for prospects with legitimate deployment-delay reasons — website redesigns, upcoming launches, staff training windows, vacations. It preserves founders club economics without pressuring activation. Worth being the default answer to "we’re not ready to deploy yet" from this point forward.
Strong
Honest integration answer on patient now — named the personal connection without overreaching
When Carrie asked about patient now experience at 8:50, Stefanie gave the strongest possible credibility answer: "my VP’s wife is the director of client success at patient now. If you need any help there, he has … I literally was yelling up to her." Then she followed with the practical answer: most practices use the request-an-appointment flow rather than direct booking, because it gives the practice a moment to handle the lead live while capturing what the patient is actually interested in. That’s a sharper answer than just "we integrate" — it names the specific workflow most practices choose and why.

The Kerrigan (HIPAA-compliant) vs Zapier distinction at 10:48 was also well-executed — important for a prospect working across patient now + growth 99 + go high level. That’s a three-system stack that requires the HIPAA-compliant bridge, not the quick-and-dirty one.
The "my VP’s wife runs CS at patient now" detail is a genuine credibility asset for patient now prospects specifically. Worth noting internally — any patient now account should route through someone who can drop that reference naturally. It’s a trust accelerator that can’t be manufactured.
Strong
Demo environment link sent live during the call — removed the provider objection
Jennifer surfaced the real blocker at 7:02: "is there a way for my provider to try this out? She’s obviously going to fight this a little bit." That’s a decision-maker concern disguised as a feature request — the provider is the gate, and Jennifer needs her to self-experience the tool before approving. Stefanie had the answer ready because the team had just been issued demo environment links the same day ("they literally just sent that, they created that and sent it on to us"). She sent the link live during the call, which turns a potential multi-day delay into an immediate next step.
The demo environment link is the right answer for any prospect with a skeptical provider or clinical gate. Route it during the call itself rather than promising to send it after — in-call delivery removes the follow-up friction.
What could go sharper
Gap
Jennifer mentioned "final stamp of approval" — the real decision-maker never got named
Jennifer closed the call at 17:02 with "I just have to get the final stamp of approval." Stefanie acknowledged and moved to the no-contract reassurance — but didn’t ask the obvious question: who gives that stamp, and can we get on a 15-minute call with them directly? Carrie was on the call, but Jennifer’s phrasing suggests Carrie is not the final DM either (otherwise the decision could have happened live). That means there’s a third stakeholder somewhere who hasn’t been engaged yet.

This is the exposed-DM variant — two internal advocates are on the call but the actual commit authority is still upstream. Continuing via email-only follow-up into a third decision-maker is how deals stall for 2-3 weeks past the founders-club window.
The next move: text or email Jennifer within 24 hours with a specific ask — "I’d love to loop in the final decision-maker on a 10-minute call before the founders club window closes. Would Thursday or Friday work?" The sign-up-and-pause lever removes deployment pressure, but the founders club deadline is still a legitimate commitment accelerator for this shape of deal.
Gap
Growth 99 / patient now / go high level — three-system stack was acknowledged but not stress-tested
Carrie named the full integration picture at 11:32 — patient now as the EMR, go high level as the CRM, growth 99 as the incoming website platform. That’s three systems, each with different integration paths through Kerrigan or Zapier. Stefanie confirmed integration works but didn’t walk through the specific data flow — which lead fields route where, what happens at the handoff, where the practice will see the consolidated view.

For a practice mid-website-rebuild on growth 99, this is a real operational question. The deployment is not just embedding a link — it’s designing the lead-routing architecture across three systems.
When prospects name three or more systems in their integration stack, offer a dedicated 20-minute technical call with onboarding rather than answering live. "Let me set you up with our implementation team — they’ll walk through exactly how leads route across the three systems and confirm the architecture before you sign." That converts an abstract "it integrates" reassurance into a concrete deployment plan, which is what a careful operator like Carrie actually needs.
The broader signal
Playbook contribution
This tape is why the sign-up-and-pause play is now named in the playbook
Stefanie’s sign-up-and-pause move at 7:50 was the first time this specific closing lever was documented on a recorded call. Before this tape, the move existed in Phil’s Slack messages and in one-off rep improvisations. After this tape, it’s a named play with concrete example dates (May 11, June 11) and a clean scripted delivery ("sign up with that 499 price and then we are just creating a document and giving it to onboarding saying they don’t want this released").

This is how the sales motion matures — calls like this one surface moves that then become standard coaching. The Sign-up-and-pause pattern card in the War Room traces directly back to this 18-minute follow-up.
Lessons from the call
What the tape taught us about deployment-delay objections:
Sign-up-and-pause is now the default answer. Founders pricing locked today, unlimited clock starts when the practice is actually ready. Named example dates make the move feel real to the prospect.
What the tape taught us about multi-system integrations:
When three or more systems are named (patient now + growth 99 + go high level), route to onboarding for a dedicated architecture call rather than answering live. Use Kerrigan for HIPAA-compliant bridges, not Zapier.
What the tape taught us about provider gates:
Demo environment links sent live during the call remove the follow-up friction. Any prospect with a skeptical clinical provider should leave the call with a working demo link in hand, not a promise to send one.
What Stefanie did right under real conditions:
Surfaced the sign-up-and-pause lever without being asked, leveraged the patient now CS connection credibly without overreaching, delivered the demo environment link live, reassured on no-contract at the close. Solo follow-up call, no VP present, strong self-sufficiency.
The honest read:
This deal is likely to close on founders pricing pending the provider demo — the sign-up-and-pause removes the deployment friction and the demo link removes the provider-skepticism friction. The only remaining risk is the unnamed third decision-maker behind Jennifer’s "final stamp of approval." The 24-hour follow-up move is to engage that person directly.

Pre-visualized, scored, enriched patients. Not cold leads. Not form fills. Not shared contacts.

Close variants — pick the right one
Waitlist hold.
For prospects ready-in-principle but not ready-in-timing (hiring, travel, website unfinished). Sign up today, card on file, founders club swag/community immediate, activation delayed. 7+ documented wins.

Sign-up-and-pause.
Newer variant from Carrie/Stefanie follow-up. Activate the account, then pause billing at the end of month one if they haven't deployed yet. Fit: prospects with real operational readiness gaps who want in but can't start generating leads day one.

Refund safety net.
For soft-approval-gate closes (spouse, business partner, office manager review). "$499, if [person] hates it, we'll refund it." Converts approval dependency into low-risk test. Mandy / Vitality Health.

Event deadline acceleration.
When prospect has a live event in under a week. Escalate internally visibly on the call (Slack Phil/CTO live), compress the close into the same session. Dusan / deRMA.

Founders club extension.
For "let me think about it" with legitimate internal review timeline. VP-authority move: "The special runs through Friday, but if you can commit by Monday I can push it." Only for prospects with real intent. Michell / Cosmetic Surgical Arts.

Abbreviated product demo focused on fit for their client base. Skip standard discovery. State referral economics explicitly. Loop in Alexandra (referral manager) via text on the call. Offer co-pitch support so the partner doesn't have to become an Ageless expert themselves.

QR code on a presentation slide + custom-tracked demo link routes event attendees through the Ageless experience and tags them to the referral partner. Works for consultant events, patient open houses, new location launches, and conference talks.

EntityMed
White-labeled AI facial simulator + built-in CRM + Google Ads integration
Direct competitor
$499+/mo
▶
Positioning:
Direct competitor — facial simulator with basic CRM; Ageless AI is a full acquisition and retention engine with clinical credibility and a loyalty flywheel EntityMed cannot replicate
Ageless advantages
1-5 star lead scoring with income estimation and intent data
Beauty Score + Future Aging Self — no EntityMed equivalent
Existing patient reactivation — EntityMed is acquisition-only
Full RepeatMD ecosystem: loyalty, rewards, memberships, financing
15-physician Medical Advisory Board incl. Dr. Paul Nassif
4,000+ practices, $50M raised, $3B+ revenue generated for clients
EntityMed weaknesses
Curiosity-driven leads with no budget, timeline, or intent signals
One case study: 120 leads, ~$25K over 2 months

Talk track
EntityMed is the most direct competitor we face, and the gap is significant. They built a simulator that captures emails — people give their info to play with a filter, not because they are ready to buy. There is no lead scoring, no income enrichment, no budget qualification. Your staff gets a list of names and spends hours sorting tire-kickers from real buyers. Their one published case study is 120 leads in a weekend that generated roughly $25K over two months. Ageless AI scores every lead 1 to 5 stars with income estimation, treatment interest, and engagement data before it ever hits your CRM. High-scoring leads are fast-tracked. Lower-scoring leads are nurtured automatically. And that is just the front door — behind it is the entire RepeatMD platform: loyalty, rewards, memberships, financing, AI advisors. EntityMed gives you leads. Ageless gives you patients.

Do say
- EntityMed captures name and email before qualifying anyone. People engage out of curiosity, not purchase intent. Ageless pre-qualifies before the visualization and scores every lead with income and intent data.
- Their one case study is 120 leads that generated $25K over 2 months. Ask them what happened to the other 95+ that never converted.
- EntityMed is a standalone simulator. Once a lead comes in, the practice is on its own to convert and retain. Ageless feeds patients directly into the RepeatMD loyalty and rewards flywheel.
- EntityMed uploads patient facial photos to Google Firebase and shares with third-party business partners per their own privacy policy. Worth asking where those photos actually go.
- We have 15 board-certified physicians including Dr. Paul Nassif validating our visualizations. EntityMed's own terms say they are not a health care provider.

Don't say
- EntityMed's visualizations don't work — they do produce facial simulations, just with narrower treatment scope and no clinical validation.
- Their Google Ads integration is worthless — it is a real feature, just a blunt instrument with no audience refinement or optimization controls.
- They have no customers — they have clients, just minimal public proof and one heavily recycled case study.
- Their CRM doesn't work — it is basic but functional. The issue is what it is missing: scoring, enrichment, and ecosystem depth.

EntityMed-specific objections
"We're already using EntityMed."
▶
Got it. How has the lead quality been? What we hear from practices that switched is that EntityMed generates volume, but the leads are not scored or enriched. Your team ends up spending hours chasing people who just wanted to play with a filter. Ageless AI scores every lead 1 to 5 stars with income estimation and treatment intent before it ever hits your CRM. Your staff knows exactly who to call first. Plus, EntityMed is just a simulator. Ageless plugs into the full RepeatMD growth engine: loyalty, rewards, memberships, financing, AI advisors. It is not a widget. It is a patient acquisition and retention platform.
"EntityMed is cheaper."
▶
EntityMed starts at $499/month for a simulator and a basic CRM. But what is the cost of bad leads? If your front desk spends 20 hours a month chasing unqualified leads at $25/hour, that is $500 in wasted labor on top of the subscription. Ageless pre-qualifies and scores every lead, so your team only spends time on patients who are ready to buy. And you are not just getting a simulator — you are getting the full RepeatMD ecosystem. The ROI conversation is completely different.
"EntityMed got us 120 leads in one weekend."
▶
That is their headline case study — and it is the only one they have. But how many of those 120 actually booked? They reported $25K in revenue over two months. At $500-$1,000 per treatment, that is 25-50 conversions max. What happened to the other 70-95 leads? With Ageless, every lead comes in with treatment goals, budget signals, and a quality score. You do not need 120 leads if 30 of them are pre-qualified and ready to book.
"We just need a simulator, not a whole platform."
▶
A simulator generates interest. Then what? EntityMed hands you a list of names and says good luck. There is no scoring, no enrichment, no automated nurture, no loyalty loop. Your staff becomes the entire conversion engine. Ageless handles the full journey: qualification, scoring, nurture, and then feeds those patients into RepeatMD's loyalty and rewards system so they keep coming back. The simulator is the entry point, not the product.
"What about patient data privacy?"
▶
EntityMed uploads patient facial photos to cloud servers and their privacy policy allows sharing with third-party business partners. Ageless was built with AWS and RepeatMD's existing HIPAA-conscious infrastructure. For practices that care about patient data security, this is a meaningful difference. Worth asking EntityMed exactly where patient photos are stored and who has access.

Perfect Corp is an enterprise AR company whose core business is beauty/retail try-on (Sephora, Ulta, ecommerce brands). Ageless is a patient acquisition engine that captures, scores, and pre-sells prospects before they ever book a consultation. Different jobs, not competing products.
Ageless advantages
Lead capture first — Ageless runs on your website as acquisition; Perfect Corp runs in-practice as consultation aid

Future Aging Self — the "what you look like in 15 years if you do nothing" emotional peak that closes deals

Perfect Corp gaps — for a med spa's job to be done

Talk track
Perfect Corp is an enterprise AR company. Their core business is beauty retail — they power the try-on experiences for Sephora, Ulta, and ecommerce brands. They have built tools for med spas — a face reshape simulator, a skin diagnostic, a skincare aesthetic simulator — and some of them are well-built consultation aids. I want to be honest about that. But they were built for a different job than ours. Perfect Corp's tools live inside the consultation, enhancing the conversation you already have with a patient sitting in front of you. Ageless is built for everything that happens before the consultation — capturing website visitors who weren't going to call, scoring them by income and intent, pre-selling them with visualization and Future Aging Self, and handing your team an enriched lead who already wants the treatment. Perfect Corp makes consultations better. Ageless makes sure the consultations happen in the first place. For a practice that already fills its calendar, a consultation tool helps the conversations convert. For a practice that needs more bookings, the job starts upstream — and that's what we built.

Do say
- Perfect Corp is an AR company — their core business is retail beauty (Sephora, Ulta, ecommerce). They have med spa products, and some are well-built, but they were designed as consultation enhancement tools, not as a patient acquisition engine.
- "Perfect Corp makes consultations better. Ageless makes sure the consultations happen in the first place."
- Their tools live in your practice during the consult. Ours lives on your website, in your Instagram bio, at your events — capturing visitors before they ever contact you.
- We score every lead 1-5 stars with income and intent data. Their tools produce an image for a patient who's already in your chair. We produce a ranked lead before they've committed to booking.
- You're not choosing between two acquisition tools — you're deciding whether you want a better consultation or a better way to fill your consultation calendar. Most practices that succeed with Ageless still run consultations the way they always have; we just make sure more happen.
- Their med spa products run on annual enterprise contracts. Ageless is $499 first month, month-to-month, cancel inside the product. Completely different commitment shape.

Don't say
- "Perfect Corp only does makeup try-on" — they have real med spa products (AI Face Reshape Simulator, Skincare Pro Aesthetic Simulator). Dismissing their capability makes you look uninformed and hands the prospect a reason to doubt you on everything else.
- "Their clinical validation is weak" — they have a Wake Forest University study validating their AI Skin Diagnostic against physician assessments. Attack the positioning, not the credentials.
- "They're retail, we're medical" — too reductive. The real answer is they're consultation-side, we're acquisition-side. Different jobs.
- "They don't care about med spa" — they have a dedicated product line for the category. They care. They just approach it from the consultation-enhancement angle, which is not our angle.

Perfect Corp-specific objections
"We already use Perfect Corp in the consultation room."
▶
Perfect. Then you have the consultation side covered. The question is what's bringing patients into the consultation in the first place. Perfect Corp runs once the patient has already walked through the door — we run on your website, your Instagram bio, your ads, to turn the visitors you're already paying for into booked consultations. The two tools aren't competing; they're on different halves of the funnel. How are you filling the calendar that Perfect Corp is helping you convert?
"Perfect Corp has a face reshape simulator too — what's different?"
▶
Both tools simulate treatments. The difference is everything around the simulation. When a patient finishes a visualization with Ageless, we've captured their contact info, scored them 1-5 stars based on income and treatment intent, enriched their profile, and started an automated follow-up sequence tied to exactly what they explored — all before a staff member picks up the phone. Perfect Corp's simulators are consultation aids; they improve the conversation when the patient is already in front of you. Our job is making sure that conversation happens in the first place.
"They're more established — we trust a bigger company."
▶
Perfect Corp is a great company — they've built enterprise AR products for Sephora, Ulta, and dozens of global beauty brands. Their core business is retail. Our parent company RepeatMD is purpose-built for medical aesthetics: 4,000+ practices, $50M raised, $3B+ in revenue generated for our clients, 15-physician advisory board led by Dr. Nassif. For a med spa specifically, we're the deeper specialization. Perfect Corp builds for beauty retail as their primary market. We build for your industry as our only market.
"Perfect Corp runs in-practice on an iPad — can you do that?"
▶
Yes — Ageless runs on any device with a camera. You can deploy it on an iPad in the waiting room as a QR code, use it in the consultation room as a visualization tool, put it on your website for lead capture, embed it in your Instagram bio. Same tool, multiple deployment surfaces. The in-practice use case is a subset of what Ageless does, not the core of it. If in-practice is all you want, you're only using a fraction of what you're paying for.
"We got a quote from Perfect Corp — it was expensive."
▶
That tracks with what we hear. Perfect Corp runs enterprise contracts with custom pricing and annual commitments. Ageless is $499 for an unlimited first month, no contract, cancel inside the product whenever you want. We're a different commitment shape — you can test us for a month without a procurement process, and decide based on actual results rather than a sales cycle.

Talk track
Aura Reality is impressive hardware — the 3D digital twin from 13+ cameras is genuinely a novel consult experience. But it lives entirely inside your practice. The patient has to already be in your chair to see it, which means it can't do anything to solve the acquisition problem. The 8 out of 10 patients who want treatment but never book? Aura will never reach them. Ageless shows patients their own transformation from their own phone — before they ever contact you. By the time they walk in, the sale has already begun. And when they do walk in, Aura is capex plus ongoing fees for one use case; Ageless is $499 a month, no contract, plugged into the full RepeatMD flywheel — loyalty, rewards, memberships, financing, AI advisors. Aura is a great consult room upgrade. Ageless is how you fill the room.

Do say
- Aura Reality is genuinely impressive in the consult room — but it needs the patient already in your chair to work at all. Ageless reaches patients on their phone before they ever contact you.
- Aura is a capital expenditure plus monthly fees for one use case. Ageless is $499 a month, no contract, plugged into your entire acquisition and retention stack.
- Every Ageless lead arrives scored 1-5 stars with income estimation, job title, and treatment intent. Aura delivers a digital twin and hands the rest back to your staff.
- The acquisition problem is not at the consultation — it is 90% of patients never reaching the consultation. Ageless operates at that layer. Aura cannot.
- Think about what Aura actually replaces: it replaces a provider narrating a before/after photo. Ageless replaces the entire gap between curiosity and booking.

Don't say
- Aura's imaging is inferior — the 3D capture quality is genuinely strong, that is their real strength.
- Patients don't like Aura — the in-practice experience actually impresses patients who see it.
- You should replace Aura with Ageless — if a practice has already bought Aura, they solve different problems.
- Aura has no customers — they have real practices using the system, it's just a very different funnel stage.

Aura Reality-specific objections
"We just invested in Aura."
▶
Great — keep it. Aura is a consultation room tool and it will keep improving your closing rate for patients who are already in your chair. But ask yourself how those patients got into your chair in the first place. Ageless reaches the 90% who never made it that far — they hesitated, they researched, they disappeared. Ageless shows them their own face transformed on their own phone and scores them for your team before they ever book. The two tools don't compete — Aura closes, Ageless fills. Together the conversion math changes completely.
"Aura has 3D imaging — Ageless is just a phone app."
▶
Correct — and that is the point. The patient's phone is where the buying decision starts. Aura requires the patient to physically be in your practice, in front of a 13-camera rig. Ageless meets them where they already are, with the acquisition-stage experience they will actually engage with. The goal is not to out-specify Aura on hardware — it is to operate in a layer Aura cannot reach.
"Isn't a 3D twin more impressive than a photo edit?"
▶
For in-person consultations, absolutely — and Aura will do that job well. But the impressive moment has to happen at the buying decision, which happens on a phone. Most patients never get to the consult room for Aura to impress them. Ageless creates the impressive moment first, then your staff leverages that interest — and if you have Aura, the in-room experience becomes the close, not the introduction.
"What about data — does Aura do what Ageless does on the backend?"
▶
Aura captures imaging data for clinical consult purposes. It does not enrich leads, score them, feed automated nurture sequences, or plug into loyalty and rewards systems. Ageless delivers every lead with income estimation, job title, intent signal, star score — and then feeds qualified patients into the full RepeatMD ecosystem: memberships, rewards, financing, AI advisors. Different data entirely, different purposes.
"The founder of Aura says AI face apps can't match 3D clinical accuracy."
▶
True for surgical planning and clinical documentation — and we don't compete there. But the buying conversation isn't about clinical accuracy, it's about helping the patient imagine themselves. That's a marketing problem, not a clinical one. Ageless is built for the marketing problem; Aura is built for the clinical one. Practices buy Aura for the consult room, they buy Ageless for everything upstream of it.

- Different budget lines: Aesthetics Pro is operations; Ageless is marketing and acquisition.

Don't say
- Aesthetics Pro is bad software — it works well for practice management.
- You should replace Aesthetics Pro — totally different function, they don't overlap.
- Aesthetics Pro is too expensive — that's an operational line item, not a marketing one.
- Our tool does what Aesthetics Pro does — we don't do EMR or scheduling, and we shouldn't.

Aesthetics Pro-specific objections
"We already use Aesthetics Pro."
▶
Great — keep it. It runs your practice. Ageless doesn't replace practice management software; we're patient-facing AI for acquisition and conversion. Aesthetics Pro handles patients after they're in your system. Ageless reaches them before.
"Aesthetics Pro has photo storage — isn't that the same?"
▶
Photo storage is archival, for existing patients. Ageless's AI visualization is pre-booking — it shows prospective patients their own face transformed to drive intent. Same medium, completely different purpose and audience.
"We can't afford another monthly tool."
▶
Aesthetics Pro lives in your operational budget; Ageless should live in your marketing budget. The ROI math for each is different. Ageless earns against new patient revenue — if it drives two additional consults a month, it has paid for itself. That's not the same as adding another operational cost.
"Will Ageless integrate with Aesthetics Pro?"
▶
Lead routing from Ageless works across integration bridges like Kerrigan (HIPAA-compliant) and Zapier, which can push scored leads into downstream systems. For specific Aesthetics Pro setups, our onboarding team can walk through the routing architecture.
"Aesthetics Pro is an 'all-in-one' — do we need Ageless too?"
▶
All-in-ones tend to be all-in-one for practice management, which is what Aesthetics Pro is. They are not all-in-one for patient acquisition — that's a separate discipline, and it needs a dedicated tool. Ageless is built for that job specifically.

Talk track
RealSelf is a consumer aesthetic marketplace — patients research treatments, read reviews, and request consultations from listed providers. It's a legitimate distribution channel and plenty of practices use it. But there are two structural issues: first, the patient is comparing you to other providers side-by-side, which puts you in a pricing and review race you don't control. Second, the patient relationship belongs to RealSelf, not to you — they market to that patient going forward. Ageless flips both. Patients experience the visualization under your brand, on your site. The lead arrives scored with income and intent data, in your CRM, with no competitive comparison in the discovery moment. And because Ageless is plugged into RepeatMD, the patient relationship becomes yours to retain via loyalty, memberships, and financing. RealSelf is a channel you rent. Ageless is infrastructure you own.

Do say
- RealSelf's patients are comparison-shopping you against other listed providers. Ageless patients are experiencing your brand directly.
- RealSelf leads arrive with a name and message. Ageless leads arrive with income estimation, intent signals, and a 1-5 star score.
- RealSelf owns the patient relationship — they market to those patients forever. Ageless patients are yours from the first click.
- RealSelf's visibility is pay-to-play and review-dependent. Ageless's visibility lives on your own website and social — no listing battle.
- Think of RealSelf as a rented channel and Ageless as owned infrastructure. Both can exist, but only one compounds in your favor over time.

Don't say
- RealSelf is a waste of money — for some practices it is a legitimate source of consults.
- RealSelf patients are low quality — they are real patients with real intent, just with structural channel issues.
- You should drop RealSelf — keep it if it works for you, but don't rely on it alone.
- RealSelf's reviews are fake — they're subject to the same issues as any review platform, but generally legitimate.

RealSelf-specific objections
"RealSelf already sends us leads."
▶
Keep RealSelf if it's working — we're not asking you to drop it. We're asking you to also own the visualization and acquisition layer on your own site. RealSelf leads come with minimal data and are marketplace-competitive. Ageless leads arrive scored, enriched, and brand-exclusive to you. Adding Ageless doesn't replace RealSelf; it makes your total acquisition stack stronger.
"We get good consultations from RealSelf."
▶
Good — that's valuable. Now think about the patients you're losing on your own website because there's no AI visualization experience. Those patients bounce. Ageless captures them on your site, scores them, and feeds them to your team. You'd have the RealSelf channel working plus your own website actually converting traffic.
"RealSelf is cheaper per lead."
▶
RealSelf looks cheaper per lead because the leads arrive unqualified and you spend time triaging. Every unqualified consult eats staff hours at $25-$50 an hour. Ageless leads arrive scored 1-5 stars with income and intent — your staff only engages with high-scoring leads ready to book. The math on true cost per qualified lead usually reverses once you calculate staff time.
"Patients trust RealSelf reviews."
▶
Patients trust the review mechanism, yes — but they don't trust RealSelf's brand, they trust the specific reviews of specific providers. That trust is built on your reviews, which you've earned. You can translate that same trust into your own site by pointing new patients to your website where Ageless's visualization experience lets them engage deeply with your practice before they ever request a consult.
"RealSelf owns the relationship anyway — what does Ageless change?"
▶
Exactly the point. RealSelf owns the patient relationship, which means they market to your patients going forward, sometimes on behalf of your competitors. Ageless gives you direct ownership — your brand, your site, your CRM, your retention loop via RepeatMD. Over a year or two, the compounding difference in LTV is significant.

Acquisition Deep Dive
How medspas get traffic, where that traffic lands, and why most of it never becomes a patient
Most medspa owners think about marketing as two things: how much they're spending and how many leads they're getting. The real question is what happens in between — where traffic comes from, where it lands, and what the landing experience actually does to convert intent into a booked patient. This section maps the full acquisition chain so your team can run a sharper discovery conversation and position Ageless exactly where it belongs: as the conversion layer that makes every traffic source work harder.
📡
Traffic Sources
Where patients come from — and what they cost, how warm they are, and what that means for conversion
📘
Meta Paid (Facebook & Instagram)
Paid — demand generation
CPL:
~$22–$43
CPM:
~$12–$15
Results:
Days
Intent:
Low–Medium
The highest-volume lead gen channel for most medspas. Meta excels at demand generation — reaching patients who aren't yet searching but are receptive to the right creative. Traffic is cold by nature: someone scrolling Instagram didn't wake up thinking about Botox. Creative fatigue is the biggest cost driver. When ads stop feeling fresh, CPMs climb and conversion rates collapse. The landing destination is everything here — cold traffic sent to a generic lead form bleeds budget. Sent to an Ageless patient experience, it converts.

Discovery questions
Are you running Meta ads right now? What are you sending that traffic to?
What's your current cost per lead, and how many of those leads actually book?
How quickly does your team follow up when a Meta lead comes in?
Have you seen your CPMs creep up as your creative gets older?
🔍
Google Paid (Search & Display)
Paid — high intent capture
CPC:
$2.62–$15+
Conv. rate:
3–10%
Results:
Days
Intent:
High
Google Search captures patients who are actively looking — "Botox near me," "lip filler [city]," "medspa consultation." This is the highest-intent traffic a practice can buy. CPCs are higher than Meta ($5–$15+ in competitive markets like NYC or LA), but so is conversion readiness. The problem is what happens after the click. A patient who searched "Botox near me" and lands on a generic homepage or lead form loses momentum immediately. Treatment-specific landing pages with a strong next step — like an Ageless visualization — convert this traffic dramatically better than generic destinations.

Discovery questions
Are you running Google Search campaigns? Which treatments?
Where does that traffic land — your homepage, a treatment page, or a dedicated landing page?
What's your cost per booked consultation from Google, not just cost per click?
Are you tracking phone calls as conversions, or just form fills?
🌱
SEO / Organic Search
Organic — long-term asset
Cost:
$1,500–$5,000/mo agency
Timeline:
3–6 months
Intent:
Medium–High
Longevity:
Compounds
SEO is the long game — and for medspas, it's one of the highest-ROI channels over a 12–24 month horizon. Practices that rank for "Botox [city]" or "best medspa near me" get traffic without paying per click. The challenge is time: most practices need 3–6 months before meaningful organic traffic arrives, which is why Google Ads is the short-term complement. SEO traffic tends to skew higher intent than paid social — someone who found you through a search was looking. The landing page still matters enormously. A strong organic ranking sending traffic to a weak homepage wastes the investment.

Discovery questions
Do you know where you rank for your core treatments in your market?
Are you working with an SEO agency, or is organic search something you haven't invested in yet?
What percentage of your website traffic comes from organic search vs paid ads?
When someone finds you organically, what's the first thing they see — and what are they supposed to do next?
📱
Organic Social (Reels, Stories, TikTok, Linktree)
Organic — warm audience
Cost:
Time only
Intent:
Medium–High (warm)
Trust:
Highest
Volume:
Unpredictable
Organic social is underrated as an acquisition channel and misunderstood as a conversion tool. A follower who watches a provider's Reels consistently, trusts them, and then clicks the profile link is one of the warmest leads in the entire funnel — warmer than paid traffic by a wide margin. The problem is where they land. Most practices send profile link traffic to a Linktree that points to a homepage, a booking page, or a generic "contact us." That friction kills the conversion. A patient who was emotionally ready to act bounces because there was nothing compelling on the other side of the click. Ageless turns that profile link into a conversion engine — the warmest traffic you have meets the most engaging experience you can offer.

Discovery questions
Are you or your providers posting Reels or Stories consistently? What kind of engagement are you seeing?
What's in your profile link right now — a Linktree, your website, a booking page?
When a follower clicks that link, what are they supposed to do next — and how many actually do it?
Are you driving social traffic into any kind of qualification or follow-up sequence, or does it just land on a page and disappear?
🎯
Where Traffic Lands
The conversion layer — what patients see after the click, and what that does to your acquisition cost
📋
Lead Form
Name, email, phone — the most common medspa destination
Conversion
★★☆☆☆
▶
What works
- Fast to build and deploy on any page
- Integrates directly into most CRMs
- Low friction for highly motivated patients
- Works on Meta as a native lead ad format

What doesn't
- No emotional engagement before submission — cold traffic stays cold
- Zero qualification — name and email tell you nothing about intent or budget
- High ghost rate — people submit and never respond to follow-up
- No differentiation from the three other practices running the same form
- Requires fast human follow-up to convert — the average response time in healthcare is 47 hours; conversion drops 80% after 5 minutes

The gap:
A lead form captures contact info. It does nothing to create desire, qualify intent, or give the patient a reason to choose you over anyone else. You pay to get the click, then you pay again in staff time to chase someone who may have been casually curious. Ageless sits in front of the form — patients visualize their result first, then submit. The same form gets dramatically warmer leads.
✏️
Skin Quiz (No AI visualization)
Treatment recommendation quiz — engagement without commitment
Conversion
★★★☆☆
▶
What works
- Higher engagement than a plain lead form — interactive feels personalized
- Captures treatment intent and concern areas before the lead submits
- Works well for email nurture sequences based on quiz answers
- Lower bounce rate than a static page

What doesn't
- Recommendations are generic — patients still don't see themselves in the result
- No emotional commitment — intellectual interest is not the same as desire
- No lead scoring or income enrichment — you know their concerns, not their readiness
- No automated follow-up tied to specific answers in most implementations
- Completion rates drop sharply after 5+ questions

The gap:
A skin quiz is better than a form but stops short of the finish line. It tells a patient what treatment they might need — it doesn't show them what they'll look like with it. That last step, seeing their own face, is what creates the emotional commitment that drives a booking. Ageless delivers both: the personalized recommendation and the visual proof.
🤖
EntityMed Simulator
AI facial simulator — curiosity driver without a qualification layer
Conversion
★★★☆☆
▶
What works
- Visual engagement is genuinely higher than forms or quizzes
- Patients interact longer before submitting contact info
- Can generate high lead volume from paid campaigns
- Built-in basic CRM captures contact info

What doesn't
- Leads are curiosity-driven — people upload a selfie to play, not because they're ready to buy
- No lead scoring — all leads treated equally regardless of intent
- No income enrichment — staff has no idea who can afford treatment
- Their own case study: 120 leads in a weekend, ~$25K over 2 months — most never converted
- No patient reactivation workflow — acquisition only
- No loyalty or retention integration — dead end after the lead
- Patient photos stored on Google Firebase, shared with third parties per their privacy policy

The gap:
EntityMed generates volume. Ageless generates patients. The difference is what happens after the visualization — scoring, enrichment, automated nurture, and the full RepeatMD loyalty flywheel. EntityMed gives practices a list of names. Ageless gives them a pipeline.
🪞
Perfect Corp Simulators
Enterprise AR company — consultation-enhancement tools for inside the practice
Conversion
★★★☆☆
▶
What works
- Legitimate med spa product line — AI Face Reshape Simulator, Skincare Pro Aesthetic Simulator, AI Skin Diagnostic
- Clinical validation — Wake Forest University study validated the skin diagnostic against physician assessments
- Polished, iPad-friendly consultation experience
- Broad beauty tech heritage — real R&D infrastructure behind it

What doesn't
- Built as a consultation-enhancement tool, not a lead-capture engine — it improves conversations with patients who already booked, not with visitors who haven't
- No scoring, enrichment, or intent qualification — it produces an image, not a ranked lead
- No automated follow-up tied to patient behavior
- No retention or loyalty layer — every deal starts fresh every time
- Enterprise pricing and contract structure — not a low-friction test
- Core R&D focused on retail beauty, not med spa — category extension, not flagship

The gap:
Perfect Corp makes consultations better. Ageless makes sure consultations happen in the first place. For a practice that already fills its calendar, their tools help conversations convert. For a practice that needs more bookings, the job starts upstream — on the website, in the Instagram bio, at the event — which is where Ageless runs. Different jobs, not competing products.
📞
Phone Number / Call Now
Direct call CTA — high intent, high friction, high dependency on staff
Conversion
★★★★☆
▶
What works
- Patients who call are genuinely high intent — calling takes more effort than a form fill
- Immediate human connection builds trust faster than any digital touchpoint
- No lead goes cold between form submission and follow-up — they're already on the line
- Works exceptionally well for Google Search traffic where intent is already high

What doesn't
- Only works during business hours — after-hours calls go to voicemail and often don't convert
- Completely dependent on whoever answers — one bad call kills the lead
- No scalability — call volume is limited by staff availability
- No data capture on callers who hang up or don't leave a voicemail
- No lead enrichment or scoring — you know they called, nothing else

The honest take:
Phone is actually a strong destination for high-intent Google Search traffic — don't dismiss it. The problem is coverage gaps and scalability. Ageless works alongside phone as a 24/7 alternative: patients who won't call at 9pm can still engage, visualize, and get automatically followed up with. The two work together, not against each other.
✉️
Contact Us / Email Form
The lowest-converting destination in the medspa stack
Conversion
★☆☆☆☆
▶
What works
- Captures patients who have a specific question or are highly motivated
- Low technical overhead — already on most websites

What doesn't
- Highest friction of any digital touchpoint — patients have to compose a message
- Response times are typically the slowest in the practice — often treated as low priority
- No qualification, no scoring, no engagement layer
- Email inquiries frequently get lost, misfiled, or deprioritized behind phone and CRM leads
- No emotional momentum — by the time the practice responds, the patient has moved on

The gap:
A contact us form is not a patient acquisition strategy — it's a customer service feature. Any practice sending paid traffic to a contact page is burning budget. If this is your primary conversion mechanism, the entire funnel has a structural problem before Ageless even enters the conversation.
📅
Online Booking Site (Vagaro, Boulevard, Mindbody, etc.)
Direct booking — great for committed patients, brutal for cold traffic
Conversion
★★★☆☆
▶
What works
- Eliminates phone tag for patients who know exactly what they want
- 24/7 availability — patients can book at midnight if they're ready
- Works extremely well for existing patients rebooking
- Reduces front desk workload for routine appointments

What doesn't
- Cold or warm traffic sent straight to booking will bounce — patients who aren't ready to commit won't book on the spot
- No education or visualization layer before booking — patients arrive without emotional commitment
- High no-show rates when the booking was made without sufficient engagement
- No lead capture for patients who browse the booking page but don't complete

The gap:
Booking pages work for patients who are already sold. They fail for patients who are still deciding. Most medspa traffic — especially from paid social and organic — falls into the "still deciding" category. Ageless is the bridge: visualization and qualification happen first, then the patient arrives at the booking page already committed. Ageless integrates directly with Boulevard, Vagaro, and most major booking systems.
✦
Ageless Patient Experience
AI visualization + lead scoring + automated follow-up + loyalty flywheel
Conversion
★★★★★
▶
What works
- Patients see their own face with treatments applied — emotional commitment before the consult
- Beauty Score creates gamification and organic sharing — referral engine built in
- Future Aging Self creates urgency without pressure
- Every lead scored 1–5 stars with income estimation and treatment intent before staff sees it
- Automated text and email follow-up starts the moment visualization completes — 24/7, no staff effort
- Auto-enrolls patients into RepeatMD rewards with welcome credit — retention starts at first touch
- Affirm financing shown alongside visualization — removes price objection in real time
- Works on every traffic source: paid social, Google, SEO, organic Reels, Linktree profile link
- Full pixel tracking — Meta, Google, TikTok — so ad spend optimizes toward actual visualizations

What to acknowledge
- Requires practice to share the link across their marketing channels
- Best results come when it's embedded on the website, not just a standalone link
- Staff still needs to work the high-scoring leads — Ageless qualifies, it doesn't close

The position:
Ageless is the only landing destination that does four things simultaneously: creates emotional commitment, qualifies intent, follows up automatically, and starts the retention loop. Every other destination does one of those things at best. The practices winning patient acquisition in 2025 and 2026 are using Ageless as the conversion layer on top of whatever traffic they're already running — paid or organic.
🔄
The Full Funnel View
Where most practices are leaking revenue — and where Ageless fits
Traffic arrives
A patient sees a Reel, clicks a Meta ad, searches Google, or follows a Linktree link. At this point they are curious — not committed. The quality of their intent depends heavily on the channel: Google Search traffic is highest intent, paid social is lowest, organic social falls in the middle because of the trust relationship they already have with the provider.
↓
The landing experience
This is where most medspa funnels break. A curious patient hits a lead form, a homepage, or a generic booking page and bounces — not because they weren't interested, but because nothing on the other side of the click gave them a reason to act.
The landing experience is the single highest-leverage variable in the entire funnel.
Traffic source determines who shows up. The landing experience determines who converts.
↓
Lead capture
Patients who do submit their information are a fraction of visitors. Without an engaging experience, form fill rates on cold traffic typically run 5–15%. With Ageless, patients who go through a full visualization experience submit at significantly higher rates because they have already invested time and seen a personal result — they want to know what comes next.
↓
Lead quality
A standard lead form gives staff a name and a phone number. No intent signal, no income data, no idea if this person can afford treatment or is just browsing.
Ageless enriches every lead with income estimation, job title, treatment interest, and engagement depth before anyone picks up the phone.
Staff works 5-star leads first. Lower-scoring leads enter automated nurture. No one gets lost.
↓
Follow-up speed
Patients contacted within 5 minutes are 10x more likely to convert than those contacted after an hour. The average response time for medical practices is 47 hours. Most medspas have no automated follow-up at all — leads sit in an inbox until someone gets to them.
Ageless responds in seconds.
The moment a patient completes a visualization, personalized text and email outreach starts automatically — referencing the specific treatments they explored, around the clock.
↓
The consultation
A patient who arrived through Ageless enters the consultation having already seen their result. They are not asking "will this work?" They are asking "when can we start?" The staff's role shifts from convincing to confirming. Consultation conversion rates are dramatically higher because the emotional decision was made before the patient walked in the door.
↓
Retention loop
Most practices treat acquisition and retention as separate problems. Ageless connects them at the point of first contact.
Every patient who goes through the Ageless experience is automatically enrolled in the RepeatMD rewards program with a welcome credit
— before they ever set foot in the practice. Affirm financing is shown during the visualization. The retention loop starts at the top of the funnel, not after the first visit.
The one-line summary for discovery
Most practices have a traffic problem they think is a lead problem, and a lead problem they think is a conversion problem. The actual issue is almost always the landing experience — what happens in the 60 seconds after someone clicks.
Ageless is the answer to that 60 seconds.
It makes every traffic source you're already paying for work harder, and it starts the retention relationship before the patient ever contacts you.

What worked
Strong
Remy ran clean discovery solo — service mix, acquisition, and existing database in four questions
Without Mike on the call, Remy asked four sharp discovery questions in the first two minutes: what's your specific service focus, what about non-surgical, where are you at with patient acquisition, and is your existing database more surgical or non-surgical inquiries? Dr. Wenzel revealed: facelifts are the primary focus, CO2 and Morpheus8 are high-volume non-surgical, injectables are a good part of the business, word of mouth and organic Google only, and the patient split is approximately 50/50 surgical vs. non-surgical with many coming in just wanting his opinion.
This is the strongest solo discovery performance in the dataset. Four questions, complete picture of the practice, no wasted time. The "50/50 split with patients wanting your opinion first" answer is particularly useful — it's an opening for the consultation efficiency angle that Remy correctly used later.
Strong
Remy connected the Ageless link to Dr. Wenzel's existing Instagram workflow
Dr. Wenzel mentioned he posts his own before-and-afters on Instagram and that's his primary CTA for new patients. Remy immediately reframed: "So now when you're posting those before-and-afters of others, you could include the link to your very own app where they could actually experience what their before and after would look like too." Exact right pivot — makes Ageless additive to what he's already doing rather than a replacement.
This reframe — "you're already doing before-and-afters, now you can make it personal" — is highly effective for practices that already invest in content. Worth adding to the Quick Ref tab as a hook for social-content-active practices.
Strong
Second location opening surfaced and connected to Ageless timing
Dr. Wenzel mentioned mid-call that he's opening an additional location in a larger city in mid-June or early July. Remy immediately connected this: start the ads 30 days before launch, include the Ageless link from day one, use the founders club to learn what works so the launch is optimized. This is the strongest use case in the call and Remy handled it well.
New location launches are one of the highest-urgency Ageless use cases — the practice needs patients immediately, has zero existing patient base at that location, and is already spending on ads. This should be a named use case in the tool: "Opening a second location? Ageless is how you build a waitlist before you open the doors."
Gaps
Gap
Lead selectivity concern — never fully resolved
Dr. Wenzel asked a sharp and legitimate question: if he primarily wants facelift patients, what happens if the first 50 leads of the month are all botox patients? He'd have used his entire allocation on patients he doesn't primarily want. Remy acknowledged the tool isn't selective by service type at the intake level. This is a real limitation for surgical-primary practices and the answer — "patients are often interested in multiple things anyway" — was partially correct but undersold the consultation cross-sell angle.
For plastic surgeons, the better answer is: "The tool can't filter by service type at intake, but what it does is create a conversation. A patient who comes in visualizing non-surgical results is sitting in your chair — and that's when you as the surgeon can assess whether they're actually a surgical candidate. A lot of practices find that non-surgical inquiries convert to surgical consultations at a higher rate than cold surgical leads, because the patient already trusts you."
Well handled
"What legal protection do I have if a patient says the AI promised them a result I couldn't deliver?"
Dr. Wenzel raised the most legally sophisticated objection in the entire dataset — he referenced industry conferences warning surgeons about AI visualization liability, specifically rhinoplasty outcomes where patients use AI images as legal evidence. Remy handled it in two parts: (1) the consent checkboxes protect the practice, and (2) the visualization actually reduces this risk by creating a documented, collaborative expectation-setting session in the consultation rather than leaving the patient's expectations undefined.

The second part is the stronger argument and Remy got there, but it took a while. The framing should be leading: "This actually protects you more than the status quo. Right now patients arrive with a vague idea in their head that nobody documented. With Ageless, you're sitting down together, looking at the same image, and you're the one saying what's achievable and what isn't — and that conversation is documented."
This objection will come up on every plastic surgery call. Build a tight 60-second version: (1) Three consent checkboxes before they see anything — they've agreed it's a visualization, not a guarantee. (2) The advisory board built the disclaimer language specifically for clinical settings. (3) Most importantly — this reduces your liability because you're now having a documented expectation-setting conversation at consultation, not relying on the patient's undocumented mental image. The visualization creates the conversation that protects you.
Well handled
"Can I filter leads by geographic area?"
Dr. Wenzel asked if geographic radius filtering costs more — he referenced RealSelf's model where broader reach costs more. Remy correctly explained that Ageless pricing is purely usage-based, not geography-based, and most practices choose unlimited radius. Dr. Wenzel immediately saw the upside — patients who discover him in Florida could fly up for treatment.
This is a good differentiator against RealSelf worth naming explicitly: "Unlike RealSelf, we don't charge you more for broader reach. A patient who falls in love with their visualization in Florida and flies to your practice for a facelift costs the same $10 as a local lead."
Partial
"Is there a contract or something I can look over?"
Dr. Wenzel asked three separate times for some kind of formal agreement to review. He explicitly said "even when you sign up for Facebook they give you a contract." The no-contract positioning — usually a selling point — actually created mild discomfort for a legally cautious plastic surgeon who is accustomed to formal agreements. Remy handled it by pointing to the terms and privacy policy link in the signup flow, which satisfied him, but the conversation circled back to it multiple times.
For legally cautious prospects (surgeons especially), reframe the no-contract as a feature with a different angle: "We don't require a contract from you because we want to earn your business every month. But everything you're signing up for is documented in the terms — I'll send you a direct link so you can review it before tonight." Then actually send the terms link proactively, don't wait for them to find it.
Partial
"I'm going out of the country for two and a half weeks"
Dr. Wenzel raised a genuine timing objection — he's traveling internationally, already booked out, and doesn't want to start something mid-launch that he can't manage. Remy offered the pause option correctly and connected it to the new location launch timeline. The deal was left as a link-sent-before-midnight scenario rather than a committed close.
The pause offer was right. The gap is that Remy didn't lock a specific follow-up call for when Dr. Wenzel returns. "You're back when — mid-May? Let's put 10 minutes on the calendar for when you land so we can talk about the new location launch plan. By then you'll have had the WhatsApp community for two weeks and you'll have questions." A scheduled follow-up would anchor the deal much more firmly than a midnight deadline.
Watch
Link sent, midnight deadline — deal is warm but unanchored
Remy sent a signup link during the call with a midnight Central deadline. Dr. Wenzel said "I'll look that over and get back with you." He seemed genuinely interested and said "I guess it's worth a try" — but no card was taken, no follow-up call was booked, and the deal depends entirely on Dr. Wenzel reviewing the link before midnight while managing a busy schedule and imminent international travel.
The midnight deadline is real urgency but it may not be enough for a cautious plastic surgeon who wants to review terms. Remy should text or call before 6pm to check in: "Just wanted to make sure you got the link okay and see if you had any questions on the terms before the deadline tonight." A proactive check-in converts a warm link-sent into a close.
Effective
Remy solo — strong call without VP support
This is the only call in the dataset where a rep ran the full 53-minute demo without Mike present. Remy handled discovery, the full demo, four substantive objections including a legally complex one, pricing, and the close mechanics entirely solo. The legal liability objection in particular required nuanced handling that Remy navigated competently.
This call is strong coaching material for reps building toward solo call capability. The legal liability answer is worth workshopping into a tighter version — but the overall call structure and pacing are examples the team can learn from.

Gaps
Gap

New objection — well handled
"I don't like the beauty score — getting a grade feels harsh like telling someone they're a C"
Becky's exact words at 10:51: "I don't like the part about where it scores you. I feel like you're getting a beauty grade and that feels really harsh to me... I think that's heartless." She was firm but not hostile. Zack handled it cleanly at 11:34 — "yeah, we have built that setting. So if you don't want to show the score, you just turn it off." Becky's response: "Oh good." Objection resolved in under 30 seconds. This is the second documented beauty score pushback in the dataset (Becky and earlier instances). A meaningful segment of operators have this reaction.
This objection needs its own entry in the Objections tab and should be in the standard demo flow for any operator-led (not owner-led) call. Lead with the toggle: "The score is optional — if your brand voice is 'we work with you on what YOU want, not what we think you need,' you can turn it off in settings. Most practices that are brand-forward about patient empowerment do exactly that." That framing validates Becky's values before the toggle answer, which closes the loop faster.

The single-dashboard integration answered the real concern — this isn't another system, it's an expansion of the one they already know.
For any existing RepeatMD customer, the "one dashboard" answer to staff overwhelm is the winning frame. Reps should explicitly show the integrated view during the demo, not just mention it. "You don't need to train your team on a new system. This just shows up next to what they're already doing" is the 10-word version. Works for any multi-system practice.

She wasn't sold on the visualization accuracy or the team operational fit — she was sold on the ability to test-and-cancel without commitment risk. Card came in cleanly after that exchange.
For risk-averse operators who've heard the pitch and have genuine reservations (beauty score, staff overwhelm), lead the close with the no-contract / month-to-month / cancel-inside-product framing rather than the founders club urgency. Urgency works on the pre-sold; no-risk works on the skeptical. Becky was the latter — Zack read it correctly.

The hoodie hits for some prospects (practice-proud, brand-aware) and falls flat for others (operational skeptics like Becky). Zack didn't lose the close but the hoodie didn't add any lift either.
Read the prospect before leading with the swag. For operator-led calls where the decision is risk-based, the hoodie isn't a value-add — it can even read as trivializing. Save it for closers who've demonstrated brand affinity or who've asked about community. For Becky's type, the WhatsApp community is the founders club value, not the swag.

At 6:38, Michell volunteered: "We do use a program that is similar as far as you can show injections and what this would do and this will do, but it's not as elaborate." This is a direct competitive intelligence data point — Galderma has a consultation imaging tool deployed in this practice on iPads. Dominique's follow-up at 18:00 was sharp: "I know you mentioned the Galderma tool, you weren't too happy with it. What exactly did you feel like it was missing?" Michell clarified: "It's not that I'm not happy with it. It's that I think your program is going to offer a little bit more detail." Clean surfacing of the differentiator without badmouthing the competitor.
When a prospect volunteers a competitor tool they're already using, the move is to ask what's missing, not what's wrong. Michell's response — "it's not that I'm not happy" — was more generous than most prospects would give, and that was because Dominique asked a specific gap question rather than a general "how do you like it" question. Use this pattern for any competitor mention.
Strong
Mike correctly positioned plastic surgery timing (June launch) without losing the call
Dr. Cohn's practice does surgical AND non-surgical work. The surgical visualization launches in June. Dominique and Mike could have treated the call as a "come back in June" conversation — instead, they correctly framed the non-surgical side as the immediate opportunity and the surgical side as the expansion in two months. Dominique at 4:18: "Right now we would be able to support the non surgical side in the meantime and help grow that side. And then in June we could add in the non surgical as well." Michell explicitly named injectables as the priority growth focus at 4:26, which validated the pitch direction.
For any plastic surgery practice with both surgical and non-surgical operations, the pitch today is non-surgical. Don't wait for June. Every month they're not on Ageless for the non-surgical side is patient acquisition value lost. Mike's framing was correct but the follow-up email should include a concrete "June surgical activation" timeline so they know when that upgrade lands.
Gaps
Gap
No EMR — records stored on local server — integration path unclear
At 22:00, Michell clarified they don't have an EMR: "Everything's in house. It's all stored on our server." This is a distinct operational profile. Mike's answer was honest ("it's an image, you can just right-click it, copy it onto another doc, print it out") but that's a manual workflow, not an integration. For a practice operating off a local server without an EMR, Ageless's "integrates with Kerrigan and Zapier" pitch doesn't land — there's no destination system to integrate into.
Flag as an uncommon but real prospect profile: practices without an EMR, running on local servers. The Ageless pitch for these practices should emphasize (1) the admin dashboard as the CRM-substitute, (2) manual image export capability, (3) the messaging portal as the communication layer. Don't lead with integrations when there's nothing to integrate into.

Well handled
"We already use a Galderma tool on iPads — how is this different?"
Michell's framing was generous: the Galderma tool works but isn't elaborate enough and is location-locked to in-practice iPads. Dominique's differentiator answer was correct but could have been sharper. The clean version: "Galderma's tool lives in your practice, once the patient is already in the chair. Ageless lives on your website, in your Instagram bio, in your ads — it captures the patient before they book the consult, not after. Different jobs on the funnel." This is the same frame we use against Perfect Corp: consultation-side vs acquisition-side.
Add Galderma to the Battle Cards as a light-touch entry. Not a full competitor battle card (they're an aesthetics pharmaceutical company with a consult tool, not a competing sales-tech platform) but a short reference card so reps have specific language when the tool surfaces. Core frame: Galderma = consultation aid for patients already in the chair. Ageless = acquisition engine for visitors who haven't booked yet.
Well handled
"Are we able to print those pictures or store them somewhere else? We don't want everything stored in this."

This is an elegant use of authority — Mike visibly holds the deadline, but gives the prospect an easy way to request an extension. Michell accepted: "Very good." The close stays alive without creating fake urgency.
For any "let me think about it" close, the VP-authority move is powerful but needs to be used sparingly. It works when (a) the prospect has shown real intent, (b) the reason for delay is reasonable (internal review, not stall), and (c) the extension is limited and specific ("Monday or Tuesday" not "whenever"). Mike read all three correctly here. Reps without VP authority can do a softer version: "I'll check with my manager about extending the deal — can you give me a specific date to commit to?"

When a prospect unprompted asks about starting at a higher tier, they're telling you their volume expectation. The right follow-up is to confirm the volume and then recommend the founders club unlimited first month as the better fit. Don't just answer the tier question — use it as a close prompt.

Strong

The honest "we don't have references yet" handling is a pattern worth documenting. Every startup SaaS product faces this at launch. The answer isn't to fake references or name-drop beta partners loosely — it's to acknowledge the stage directly and pivot to what IS available (WhatsApp community, founders club, direct contact with advisory physicians). Tanya is the first primary-care-physician-running-a-med-spa in the dataset, which makes her use case distinct: she has a built-in foot traffic of primary care patients who are not yet aesthetic patients, and the waiting-room QR deployment converts that foot traffic into an aesthetic pipeline without any paid acquisition spend. The math is different from a pure med spa — she's not trying to acquire new patients, she's trying to convert existing ones into a second service line.

The deal is warm but unanchored. She's traveling, managing everything solo, and the call ended without a card. The follow-up has to be specific and fast — a generic check-in will get ignored, but a question about Athena integration details or a pre-built launch plan for May 5 re-engages her.

Priority follow-up:
